The Week: A Revealed Time Unit – Limits of Reason and Sense
Author explains how day, month, year are known by sense, but week only by revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between knowledge derived from sense/reason and knowledge derived only from revelation, using the example of the seven-day week.

Core Idea
The week is known only through revelation, not through sense or reason.

Ibn Taymiyya presents a striking epistemological argument: while days, months, and years can be known through sensory observation and rational calculation, the seven-day week is entirely dependent on prophetic revelation. He supports this claim by observing that cultures without prophetic traditions lack names for the days of the week. This lesson walks through his argument and its implications for the limits of human reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the epistemological classification
Notice how the author divides time units into two categories: those known by sense/reason (day, month, year) and those known only by revelation (week). Look for the transition phrase 'As for the week, it has no limit known by sense and reason.'
This classification is the core of the lesson.
2
Examine the evidence for the week's revealed origin
The author provides two pieces of evidence: the Quranic account of creation in six days, and the divine prescription of weekly congregational worship. These are both derived from prophetic reports.
The week's preservation is linked to religious practice.
3
Test the claim with empirical observation
The author argues that polytheistic cultures like the Turks have no names for the days of the week because they lack prophetic revelation. This serves as empirical proof that the week is not a universal rational concept.
If the week were natural, all cultures would have it.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The author concludes that 'custom follows conception' – what is not conceived cannot be known. This reinforces the dependency on revelation for some concepts.
This principle limits the scope of reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم بطلوع الفجر اليوم والشهر وهكذا أمرُ الفجر . فإن الزمان ،يوم وأسبوع وشهر وعام. فأما اليوم فيعلم بالحس والمشاهدة، وكذلك الشهر والعام يُعرف بالعدد في القمرية، وبالرؤية في الشمسية . قال تعالى: ﴿ وَلَبِثُوا فِي كَهْفِهِمْ ثَلَاثَ مِائَةٍ سِنِينَ وَازْدَادُوا تِسْعًا ﴾ [سورة الكهف : ٢٥] . كانت ثلاث مئة شمسية، وثلاث مئة وتسع هلالية . وأما الأسبوع، فليس له حد يُعرف بالحس والعقل . وإنما عُرف بأخبار الأنبياء أن الله خلق هذا العالم في ستة أيام ثم استوى على العرش. ولهذا شرع الله لأهل الملل أن يجتمعوا في الأسبوع يوماً لعبادة الله وحده، ويكون ذلك سبباً لحفظ الأسبوع الذي به يُعلم أن الله خلق هذا العالم في ستة أيام . ولهذا لا توجد أسماء الأسبوع في لغة مَنْ لا يعرفون شرائع الأنبياء، كالمشركين من الترك وغيرهم، فإنهم لا يعرفونه . والعادة تتبع التصور، فمن لم يتصور شيئاً لم يعرفه .
Knowledge of dawn, day, month, and similarly the matter of dawn. For time is day, week, month, and year. As for the day, it is known by sense and observation. Similarly, the month and year are known by number in the lunar calendar, and by sighting in the solar calendar. Allah said: 'And they remained in their cave for three hundred years and added nine.' It was three hundred solar years, and three hundred and nine lunar years. As for the week, it has no limit known by sense and reason. It is only known through the reports of the prophets that Allah created this world in six days and then established Himself on the Throne. For this reason, Allah prescribed for the people of religions to gather one day in the week for the worship of Allah alone, and that becomes a means for preserving the week by which it is known that Allah created this world in six days. Hence, the names of the days of the week are not found in the language of those who do not know the laws of the prophets, like the polytheists of the Turks and others, for they do not know it. Custom follows conception, so whoever has not conceived something does not know it.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological classification of how different units of time are known. The author states that the day is known by sense (the sight of dawn) and observation. The month and year are known by counting in lunar systems or by sighting in solar systems, citing the Quranic verse about the Companions of the Cave (300 solar years = 309 lunar years). In contrast, the week is not known by sense or reason; it is known only through the reports of prophets, specifically the account that Allah created the world in six days and then established Himself on the Throne. God prescribed weekly congregational worship as a means to preserve this knowledge. The author provides evidence: polytheistic cultures like the Turks do not have names for the days of the week because they do not have prophetic revelation. He concludes that custom (āda) follows conception (taṣawwur): what is not conceived cannot be known. This reinforces the critique against logicians who overvalue reason: some fundamental knowledge (like the week) comes only from revelation, not from rational deduction.

الأسبوع
الحس
العقل

D) By claiming that the moon's phases create a seven-day cycle.

Key Takeaway
The seven-day week is a revealed concept, not a product of sense or reason, demonstrating that revelation is an independent source of knowledge.

Critique of Unproven Astronomical Claims and the Throne
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the number of spheres and the Throne identification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's epistemological objections to Ptolemaic astronomy and evaluate his critique of identifying the Throne with the ninth sphere.

Core Idea
What the senses cannot prove, revelation alone can settle.

Ibn Taymiyya here targets two connected errors: assuming there are exactly nine celestial spheres, and equating the Throne of God with the ninth sphere. He shows both are based on weak inference, not certain knowledge. We will unpack his reasoning and see how he uses the limits of sense perception and the authority of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Find the two claims Ibn Taymiyya attacks: (1) the number of spheres is exactly nine, (2) the Throne is the ninth sphere. Note the basis he says is used for each.
2
Examine the epistemological basis
How do the astronomers claim to know there are nine spheres? Ibn Taymiyya says they infer this from variations in planetary motions and eclipses. He argues this inference is not certain ('laysa ma'luman'), and even astronomers admit more could exist.
He contrasts 'sensory' (al-hiss) with 'inferred' (mustanbat) – a key epistemological distinction.
3
Analyze the Throne identification
Some equated the Footstool (kursi) with the eighth sphere and the Throne (arsh) with the ninth, based on the prophets' mention. Ibn Taymiyya rejects this as having 'no evidence at all' (la daleela 'alayhi aslan) and being false on many grounds.
Why is this identification false? He does not list all reasons here but refers to his treatise on al-Ihata.
4
Assess the overall argument
Ibn Taymiyya's critique rests on two pillars: (a) empirical insufficiency – the inference from planetary motion does not prove exactly nine spheres, and (b) theological misapplication – equating a divine attribute with a physical model is baseless. This shows his method: reject speculative claims that lack decisive proof (burhan) and conflict with revealed truth.
This is a classic example of critical refinement – he refines the boundary between what can be known by sense, inference, and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعدد الأفلاك وكونها تسعة ليس أمراً معلوماً ولا قام دليل على أنه ليس وراء التسعة شيء، بل صرَّح أئمتهم بأنه يجوز أن تكون أشياء أخر . وهذه التسعة إنما أثبتوها بما رأوه من اختلاف حركات الكواكب. وكذلك أثبتوا لكل كوكب من الخمسة المتحيّزة عدداً من الأفلاك بسبب اختلاف حركاته وعَرَفوا ارتفاع بعضها فوق بعض بكسوف الأسفل للأعلى. وبينهم اختلاف كثير يطول وصفه في الأمور الفلكية التي لا تعرف بالحس، وكثير مما يقولونه في ذلك لا يقوم عليه دليل . ولهذا لما أخبرت الأنبياء بعرش الرب وكرسيه ظن بعضهم أن الكرسي هو الثامن، والعرش هو الفلك التاسع. وهذا القول، مع أنه لا دليل عليه أصلاً، فهو باطل من وجوه كثيرة قد بينا بعضها في مسئلة الإحاطة.
The number of celestial spheres and their being nine is not a known matter, nor has evidence been established that there is nothing beyond the nine. Rather, their own authorities have stated that it is possible that there are other things. These nine they only established from what they observed of the differences in the motions of the planets. Likewise, they established for each of the five wandering planets a number of spheres due to the difference in their motions, and they knew the elevation of some above others by the eclipse of the lower by the higher. Among them there is much difference, the description of which would be lengthy, concerning celestial matters that are not known by sense, and much of what they say about that has no proof. For this reason, when the prophets informed about the Throne of the Lord and His Footstool, some thought that the Footstool is the eighth [sphere] and the Throne is the ninth sphere. This statement, with no evidence at all, is false from many aspects, some of which we have explained in the treatise on 'al-Ihata'.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a critique of Ptolemaic astronomy's claim that there are nine celestial spheres. Ibn Taymiyya argues that this number is not definitively known, nor is there proof that nothing exists beyond nine. He notes that even the astronomers admit the possibility of more spheres. The nine spheres are inferred from observed differences in planetary motions, but such inferences are not certain. Moreover, there is much disagreement among astronomers about these celestial matters, which are not sensible. The specific error of identifying the Footstool (kursi) and Throne (‘arsh) mentioned in revelation with the eighth and ninth spheres is baseless. Ibn Taymiyya points out that this identification lacks any proof and is false for many reasons, which he claims to have elaborated elsewhere. The commentary should emphasize that Ibn Taymiyya is rejecting unfounded speculation in astronomy when it conflicts with revelatory knowledge and sensory evidence. The example is strictly from Islamic theology: the Throne and Footstool are divine attributes, not physical spheres.

Key Terms
الأفلاك
العرش
الكوكب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the basis for the claim that there are nine celestial spheres?
A) Direct sensory observation of the spheres
B) Revelation from the prophets
C) Inferences from the differing motions of planets
D) Consensus among all astronomers

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that speculative claims about the cosmos, even if widely accepted, must be distinguished from certain revealed knowledge; conflating them leads to baseless assertions about divine attributes.

?
Identify another Islamic theological claim that some have tried to support with Ptolemaic astronomy (e.g., the location of Paradise or Hell). Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, explain why such identification is problematic from an epistemological standpoint.
?

Identifying False Analogies in Logical Critique
Author criticizes logicians' false analogy about dawn and dusk lengths contradicting sensory experience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a false analogy by distinguishing between relevant and irrelevant differences, using Ibn Taymiyya's critique as a model.

Core Idea
False analogy fails when it ignores a crucial difference between two phenomena.

Ibn Taymiyya critiques the logicians' claim that dawn and dusk lengths follow the same pattern as day and night lengths. He shows that their analogy is false because they conflated the sun's movement with the behavior of its rays, which have different causes. This lesson will teach you how to spot such faulty analogies by examining the underlying differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' claim
State exactly what the logicians said: dawn in winter is shorter than in summer, and dusk in summer is shorter than in winter.
They based this on the idea that dawn is part of night and dusk is part of day.
2
Extract the analogy
Determine what is being compared: the relationship between dawn and night is analogized to the relationship between dusk and day.
The analogy is: as the length of night determines dawn length, so the length of day determines dusk length.
3
Find Ibn Taymiyya's objection
Identify the key distinction he makes: the sun's movement is celestial, while the rays depend on earthly atmospheric conditions.
This distinction breaks the analogy because the causes are different.
4
Understand the criterion for false analogy
Explain why ignoring this distinction makes the analogy false: the property (duration) is not transferred correctly because the underlying causal mechanisms differ.
Ibn Taymiyya calls this 'qiyas fāsid' (false analogy).
5
Apply the principle
What does Ibn Taymiyya say about true proofs? They do not contradict sensory experience or sound intellect. Disagreement arises only from false analogies and assumptions.
This principle helps evaluate analogies in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصاروا يقولون: حصة الفجر في الشتاء أقصر منها في الصيف، وحصة العشاء في الصيف أقصر منها في الشتاء، فإن هذه جزء من الليل وهذه جزء من النهار، فتتبعه في قدره. ولم يعرفوا الفرق بين طلوع الشمس وغروبها وبين طلوع شعاعها، فإن الشمس تتحرك في الفلك، فحركتها تابعة للفلك، والشعاع هو بحسب ما يحمله وينعكس عليه من الهواء والأبخرة، وهذا أمر له سبب أرضي ليس مثل حركة الفلك. ولهذا كان ما قالوه بالقياس الفاسد أمراً يخالفه الحس، ويعرف كذب ما قالوه باتفاق طوائف بني آدم. فالذي يعلم بالحس والعقل الصريح لا يخالفه شرع، ولا عقل، ولا حس. فإن الأدلة الصادقة لا تتعارض مدلولاتها ولكن ما يقال بقياس فاسد وظن فاسد يقع فيه الاختلاف.
And they say: the portion of dawn in winter is shorter than in summer, and the portion of evening in summer is shorter than in winter, for this (dawn) is a part of the night and that (evening) is a part of the day, so it follows it in its measure. And they did not know the difference between the rising of the sun and its setting and between the rising of its rays, for the sun moves in the sphere, its movement is dependent on the sphere, while the ray is according to what it carries and reflects from the air and vapors, and this is a matter that has an earthly cause, not like the movement of the sphere. Therefore, what they said by false analogy is a matter that contradicts sensory experience, and the falsehood of what they said is known by the agreement of all groups of humanity. So that which is known by sensory experience and sound intellect is not contradicted by law, intellect, or sensory experience. For true proofs do not have contradictory implications, but what is said by false analogy and false assumption is where disagreement occurs.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya against the logicians' (philosophers') use of false analogy (qiyas fāsid) regarding the lengths of dawn and dusk. He begins by presenting their claim: that the portion of dawn in winter is shorter than in summer, and the portion of evening in summer is shorter than in winter. They argued that since dawn is part of the night and evening is part of the day, their durations follow the lengths of night and day respectively. Ibn Taymiyya then points out their error: they failed to distinguish between the rising of the sun itself and the rising of its rays. The sun's movement is due to the celestial sphere, but the rays depend on atmospheric conditions such as vapors and reflection, which have earthly causes. Hence their qiyas is false because it compares two different things. He asserts that this false analogy contradicts empirical observation (al-ḥiss), and people universally recognize its falsehood. He then establishes a principle: what is known by sensory experience and sound intellect (al-ʿaql al-ṣarīḥ) cannot be contradicted by revelation, intellect, or sense. True proofs do not contradict each other; disagreement arises only from false analogies and false assumptions. The critique uses no sacred examples but relies on common empirical knowledge.

Key Terms
القياس الفاسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, why is the logicians' analogy about dawn and dusk lengths false?
A) Because they used a categorical syllogism in the wrong figure.
B) Because they confused the movement of the sun with the movement of its rays.
C) Because they relied on revelation rather than reason.
D) Because they ignored the agreement of all humanity.

Key Takeaway
False analogies arise when essential differences are overlooked; sound reasoning requires distinguishing between different causal mechanisms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the relevant and irrelevant features in the logicians' analogy. Construct a better analogy that would be valid for the same phenomenon (e.g., comparing the behavior of rays in different seasons based on atmospheric conditions).
?
Applying Ibn Taymiyya's principle, find a contemporary example where an analogy fails because of a missing distinction, such as in discussions of 'illah (effective cause) in usul al-fiqh.

Why the Nine Spheres Claim is Unproven
Critique of the nine-sphere claim's evidential basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two reasons Ibn Taymiyya gives for rejecting the certainty of the nine-sphere model.

Core Idea
Astronomical models are not certain truths when based on limited inference.

Ibn Taymiyya challenges the widely held assumption that there are exactly nine celestial spheres. In this passage, he points out that this claim is not known with certainty, that its evidence is indirect, and that there is disagreement among experts. This lesson unpacks his epistemological critique.

Guided Path
1
Extract the target claim
Ibn Taymiyya attacks the assertion that the number of spheres is exactly nine. Identify this claim in the Arabic.
The claim is stated at the beginning: 'كون عدد الأفلاك وكونها تسعة'.
2
Find his first objection: lack of proof
He states that it is not known and there is no proof that nothing exists beyond nine. His own scholars admit more could exist.
Look for 'ليس أمراً معلوماً ولا قام دليل' and 'يجوز أن تكون أشياء أخر'.
3
Find his second objection: method of inference
The nine spheres were inferred from planetary motion and eclipses. He notes this method is not sense-based and there is much disagreement.
Look for 'إنما أثبتوها بما رأوه من اختلاف حركات الكواكب' and 'ليس الأمر معلوماً بالحس'.
4
Summarize the critique
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that much of what they say lacks proof. The model is uncertain.
The final sentence: 'كثير مما يقولونه في ذلك لا يقوم عليه دليل'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كون عدد الأفلاك وكونها تسعة ليس أمراً معلوماً ولا قام دليل على أنه ليس وراء التسعة شيء، بل صرح أئمتهم بأنه يجوز أن تكون أشياء أخر. وهذه التسعة إنما أثبتوها بما رأوه من اختلاف حركات الكواكب. وكذلك أثبتوا لكل كوكب من الخمسة المتحيرة عدداً من الأفلاك بسبب اختلاف حركاته وعرفوا ارتفاع بعضها فوق بعض بكسوف الأسفل للأعلى. وبينهم اختلاف كثير يطول وصفه في الأمور الفلكية التي لا تعرف بالحس، وكثير مما يقولونه في ذلك لا يقوم عليه دليل. الفلك ليس العرش. ولهذا لما أخبرت الأنبياء بعرش الرب وكرسيه ظن بعضهم أن الكرسي هو الثامن، والعرش هو الفلك التاسع. وهذا القول، مع أنه لا دليل عليه أصلاً، فهو باطل من وجوه كثيرة قد بينا بعضها في مسئلة الإحاطة.
The number of spheres and that they are nine is not known, nor is there proof that there is nothing beyond nine; rather, their leading scholars stated that it is possible there are other things. These nine they only established by what they saw of the different movements of the planets. Likewise, they established for each of the five wandering planets a number of spheres due to the difference of their movements, and they knew the elevation of some above others by the eclipse of the lower by the higher. There is much disagreement among them, too lengthy to describe, concerning celestial matters that are not known by sense perception, and much of what they say about that is not supported by proof. The sphere is not the Throne. Therefore, when the prophets informed of the Lord's Throne and His Footstool, some of them thought that the Footstool is the eighth (sphere) and the Throne is the ninth sphere. This statement, while it has no proof at all, is false from many aspects, some of which we have explained in the issue of al-iḥāṭa.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya first attacks the Aristotelian claim that there are nine celestial spheres. He states that this is not known nor proven; their own leading scholars admit there could be more. The nine spheres were inferred from the observed motions of the planets, but the method is uncertain, and there is much disagreement among them. Moreover, these matters are not known by sense perception. Then he addresses a specific falsehood: some people identified the divine Throne ('Arsh) with the ninth sphere and the Footstool (Kursī) with the eighth sphere. Ibn Taymiyya emphatically rejects this: the sphere is not the Throne. The prophetic reports about the Throne and Footstool do not match the celestial model. This claim is baseless and false, as he has elaborated elsewhere. The critique uses no sacred examples here but focuses on the lack of evidence and the erroneous equation of divine and physical entities.

Key Terms
الفلك
العدد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is impossible.
B) It is possible according to their own leading scholars.
C) It is proven by revelation.
D) It is agreed upon by all astronomers.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya rejects the certainty of the nine-sphere claim by pointing to lack of proof, indirect evidence, and scholarly disagreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine the claim that the universe is 13.8 billion years old. Using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria, identify the empirical basis, any assumptions, and whether there is disagreement among scientists. Write a short critique of its certainty.
?

The Throne is Not a Celestial Sphere
Rejection of equating the Throne with the ninth sphere

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Taymiyya rejects equating the Throne (al-ʿArsh) with the ninth sphere.

Core Idea
The Throne is a revealed reality, not a physical sphere.

Some scholars identified the Throne with the ninth sphere and the Footstool with the eighth. Ibn Taymiyya emphatically rejects this identification, calling it baseless and false from many aspects. This lesson examines his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the false equation
The passage states that some people thought the Footstool is the eighth sphere and the Throne is the ninth sphere. Pinpoint this in the Arabic.
Look for 'ظن بعضهم أن الكرسي هو الثامن، والعرش هو الفلك التاسع'.
2
Find Ibn Taymiyya's rejection
He clearly says 'الفلك ليس العرش' (the sphere is not the Throne). This is a direct denial of the equation.
The phrase is the first sentence of the second part.
3
Understand his grounds
He gives two reasons: (1) there is no proof for this identification, (2) it is false from many aspects (which he elaborated elsewhere).
Look for 'لا دليل عليه أصلاً' and 'باطل من وجوه كثيرة'.
4
Connect to prophetic reports
He notes that the prophets informed of the Throne and Footstool, but the identification with spheres is not from revelation.
The phrase 'لما أخبرت الأنبياء' indicates the source of the correct understanding.

Critiquing Aristotle's Eternity of the World Argument
Ibn Taymiyya refutes Aristotle's argument for the eternity of the world, stating it contradicts the majority of philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of Aristotle's argument for the eternity of the world and distinguish between the philosophical claim of qidam al-ʿālam and Ibn Taymiyya's reinterpretation of dawām al-fāʿiliyya.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya shows that Aristotle's 'proof' actually demonstrates God's continuous activity, not the world's pre-eternity.

Ibn Taymiyya engages with the formidable claim that the world is eternal—a view he attributes specifically to Aristotle and his followers. Rather than simply dismissing it, he re-examines Aristotle's own arguments, found in his Metaphysics, and concludes that they have been misinterpreted. This lesson will guide you through Ibn Taymiyya's critical refinement: distinguishing between the philosophical doctrine of an eternal world (qidam) and the sound theological concept of God's permanent agency (dawām al-fāʿiliyya). You will learn how a rigorous critique can expose the gap between what an argument proves and what its proponents claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim under attack
First, locate the precise claim Ibn Taymiyya is refuting: Aristotle's assertion that the world is eternal (qidam al-ʿālam). Note that Ibn Taymiyya says this view is held only by Aristotle and his followers, not the majority of philosophers.
This immediately weakens Aristotle's position by showing it is not universally accepted.
2
Find Ibn Taymiyya's reinterpretation
Ibn Taymiyya states that Aristotle never had a proof for the eternity of the world; rather, his proofs only indicate 'dawām al-fāʿiliyya'—the permanence of divine agency. Understand this as saying that God is always active, not that the world always existed.
This is a classic example of critical refinement: taking an opponent's evidence and showing it supports a different conclusion.
3
Analyze the scope of the critique
Notice that Ibn Taymiyya does not stop at Aristotle. He also criticizes two groups: innovating theologians who add to revelation without proof, and philosophers (mutafalsifa) who mix truth and falsehood. Both fail to align with sound intellect and prophetic teachings.
The critique is embedded in a broader methodological stance: only the harmony of reason and revelation yields truth.
4
Assess the internal validity of Ibn Taymiyya's critique
Check whether Ibn Taymiyya's own reasoning here is sound. He claims Aristotle's arguments imply 'dawām al-fāʿiliyya' rather than qidam. Ask yourself: does the distinction hold logically? Is Ibn Taymiyya offering an alternative interpretation that is consistent with the evidence?
This step trains you to evaluate critiques critically, not accept them uncritically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجمهورهم يقولون بحدوث هذا العالم، وإنما عرف القول بقدمه من أرسطو ومتبعيه. وقد رأيت كلام أرسطو في ذلك في مقالة اللام، وهي آخر العلم الإلهي ومنتهى فلسفته وتكلمنا على ما ذكره هو وغيره من الفلاسفة، وبينا أن ما قاله خالف فيه جمهور الفلاسفة وأساطينهم، وليس معه قط دليل يدل على قدم شيء من العالم، وإنما تدل أدلته على «دوام الفاعلية» وتوابع ذلك. وقد بسطنا الكلام على ذلك في الكلام على هذا الأصل وما اضطربوا فيه. وهم المبتدعون من المتكلمين الذين يضيفون إلى الشريعة ما لم يدل عليه كتاب ولا سنة، ولا قاله أحد من سلف الأمة ولا أئمتها، فيجمعون في كلامهم بين حق وباطل والمتفلسفة في كلامهم حق وباطل وكلا الطائفتين لا يوافق ما دل عليه العقل الصريح المطابق لما جاءت به الرسل.
And the majority of them (the philosophers) say that this world is temporally originated (ḥādith). The view of its eternity is only known from Aristotle and his followers. And I have seen Aristotle's words on that in his treatise 'Lam' (the letter L), which is the last part of the Divine Science and the peak of his philosophy. And we discussed what he and other philosophers mentioned, and we showed that what he said opposes the majority of philosophers and their leaders. He never had any proof indicating the eternity of anything in the world; rather, his proofs only indicate the 'permanence of agency' and its consequences. And we have expanded the discussion on that in our discussion of this principle and what they were confused about. They are the innovators among the theologians who add to the Law what is not indicated by Book or Sunna, and which none of the Salaf or Imams said. They combine truth and falsehood in their speech, and the philosophers (mutafalsifa) also combine truth and falsehood. Both groups do not agree with what is indicated by sound intellect that conforms to what the messengers brought.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
Ibn Taymiyya addresses the philosophical claim about the eternity of the world. He notes that the majority of philosophers actually hold that the world is temporally originated (ḥādith). The view of pre-eternity (qidam) is specifically attributed to Aristotle and his followers. Ibn Taymiyya states that he has examined Aristotle's argument in his Metaphysics (Book Lambda), and he argues that Aristotle's reasoning is not a proof for the eternity of the world but rather for the 'permanence of agency' (dawām al-fāʿiliyya). He asserts that Aristotle's position contradicts the majority of philosophers. Then Ibn Taymiyya critiques both the 'innovating theologians' who add to revelation without evidence and the philosophers (mutafalsifa) who mix truth and falsehood. Neither group fully accords with sound intellect that is in harmony with prophetic teachings. The passage is a critique of both extremes.

Key Terms
قدم العالم
دوام الفاعلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what do Aristotle's arguments actually indicate?
A) The world is eternal and uncreated.
B) The world was created in time.
C) The permanence of divine agency, not the eternity of the world.
D) The existence of multiple spheres.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refines the debate on the eternity of the world by reinterpreting Aristotle's arguments as proof of God's perpetual agency, not the world's beginninglessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the following argument: 'The universe is expanding, so it must have had a beginning. Therefore, it is created.' Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, ask: Does this argument really prove a temporal beginning, or could it indicate something else (like continuous expansion from a prior state)? Identify whether the conclusion necessarily follows.
?
Find a contemporary claim that a particular scientific discovery 'proves' an ancient philosophical doctrine. Practice distinguishing between what the evidence actually indicates and what the claimant asserts—just as Ibn Taymiyya did with Aristotle.

Critique of Baseless Claims on World's Duration
Author criticizes various unfounded claims about how long the world will last after its creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flaw in analogical reasoning that extends astronomical cycles to metaphysical conclusions about the world's duration.

Core Idea
Without a sound proof, all claims about the world's remaining duration are mere conjecture.

Ibn Taymiyya here takes aim at philosophers who, despite accepting the world's temporal origination, make arbitrary claims about how long it will last. He diagnoses the root cause: they attribute all change to celestial motion and then extrapolate the world's lifespan from astronomical cycles. This lesson will teach you to recognize when an analogy is improperly extended beyond its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of criticism
Locate who Ibn Taymiyya is criticizing: the majority of philosophers who believe the world is temporally originated but then give unfounded durations.
2
Extract the analogical reasoning
What reasoning do the philosophers use? They say all events are caused by celestial motion, so they analogize the world's remaining duration to astronomical cycles.
3
Recognize the lack of evidence
Ibn Taymiyya says they have no sound proof (dalil sahih). Why is this a problem? Empirical data about astronomical cycles does not warrant conclusions about the world's total lifespan.
4
List the conflicting claims
Different groups give different numbers (12,000, 36,000, etc.). This variety indicates that there is no consensus, further evidence of baseless speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الجمهور منهم القائلون بحدوث هذا العالم تكلم منهم طوائف في بقائه وفي وقت فنائه من الروم، والهند، وغيرهم لكن بلا دليل صحيح. وسبب ذلك أنهم لم يعرفوا للحوادث التي في هذا العالم سبباً إلا حركة الفلك، وما يتجدد فيه من الأشكال، واتصالات الكواكب، فقاسوا بقاءه على ذلك فمنهم من قال: يبقى اثني عشر ألف سنة؛ ومنهم من قال: ستة وثلاثين ألف سنة؛ ومنهم من قال: ثلاث مئة ألف ألف سنة؛ ومنهم من قال: ثمانية وأربعين ألف سنة أو أربعة وعشرين ألف سنة. وكل ذلك قول بلا علم.
Then the majority of them who say that this world is temporally originated – groups among them discussed its remaining duration and its time of annihilation from the Romans, Indians, and others, but without sound proof. The reason for that is that they knew no cause for the events in this world except the movement of the sphere and what renews in it of forms and conjunctions of planets, so they analogized its remaining duration to that. Some said it remains twelve thousand years; some said thirty-six thousand years; some said three hundred thousand thousand years; some said forty-eight thousand years or twenty-four thousand years. All of that is speech without knowledge.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
Ibn Taymiyya criticizes the philosophers who, while accepting the temporal origination of the world, speculated about its duration after creation and its eventual destruction. He notes that they have no sound proof (dalīl ṣaḥīḥ). Their error stems from attributing all events solely to the movement of the celestial sphere and planetary conjunctions, and then extrapolating the world's remaining lifespan from these astronomical cycles. He then lists various numbers that different groups proposed: 12,000 years, 36,000 years, 300,000,000 years, 48,000 or 24,000 years. All these are baseless conjectures. The critique highlights the danger of using false analogies and incomplete empirical data to make claims about metaphysical realities. No sacred examples are used here; the argument is purely about the lack of evidence.

Key Terms
بقاء العالم
حركة الفلك
اتصالات الكواكب

D) They all agree on a single number.

Key Takeaway

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of the Nine Spheres and Eternity Claims
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the claim that the number of spheres is nine and criticizes the philosophers' arguments for eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and critically evaluate the two main claims Ibn Taymiyya refutes in this passage: the unprovable number of spheres and the eternity of the world.

Core Idea
No proof exists for the nine spheres or the world's eternity; Aristotle's arguments only show God's continuous agency.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya tackles two foundational claims of the philosophers: that the celestial spheres are exactly nine, and that the world is eternal. He argues that neither has any evidential support. Moreover, he links these errors to a broader problem: theologians who introduce claims into the Shari'a without evidence, and philosophers who mix truth with falsehood. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct his critique and apply his method to other arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims under attack
Find where Ibn Taymiyya states that the number of spheres is nine has no proof, and that the eternity of the world is associated only with Aristotle. Note that these are the targets of his refutation.
The claims are in the first two sentences.
2
Analyze Ibn Taymiyya's textual evidence
He claims to have read Aristotle's Lambda treatise and concluded that Aristotle's proofs do not establish eternity, only 'continuity of agency' (dawam al-fa'iliyya). Examine how he distinguishes between these two concepts.
This is a key epistemological move.
3
Link the critique to the broader epistemological error
Ibn Taymiyya groups the philosophers with the 'innovating theologians' who add to the Shari'a without evidence. He argues that both parties mix truth with falsehood and fail to align with pure reason that matches revelation.
Notice his claim that pure reason ('aql sarih) must correspond to the message of the prophets.
4
Formulate the takeaway for scientific claims
The lesson is that unsubstantiated claims—whether in astronomy or theology—must be rejected. Even Aristotle's authority does not suffice; only evidence from revelation or sound reason can support such claims.
This is a principle of critical thinking within an Islamic framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - كون عدد الأفلاك تسعة ليس عليه دليل
وجمهورهم يقولون بحدوث هذا العالم، وإنما عُرف القول بقدمه من أرسطو ومتَّبعيه . [٢٦١] وقد رأيت كلام أرسطو في ذلك في مقالة اللام، وهي آخر العلم الإلهي ومنتهى فلسفته وتكلمنا على ما ذكره هو وغيره من الفلاسفة، وبينا أن ما قاله خالف فيه جمهور الفلاسفة وأساطينهم، وليس معه قطّ دليل يدل على قدم شيء من العالم، وإنما تدل أدلته على «دوام الفاعلية» وتوابع ذلك .
وقد بسطنا الكلام على ذلك في الكلام على هذا الأصل وما اضطربوا فيه. وهم المبتَدِعُون من المتكلمين الذين يُضيفون إلى الشريعة ما لم يدل عليه كتاب ولا سنة، ولا قاله أحد من سلف الأمة ولا أئمتُها، فيجمعون في كلامهم بين حق وباطل والمتفلسفة في كلامهم حق وباطل وكلا الطائفتين لا يوافق ما دَلَّ عليه العقل الصريح المطابق لما جاءت به الرسل .
The fourth position: that the number of spheres is nine has no proof. And the majority of them say that this world is temporally originated; rather, the statement of its eternity is known only from Aristotle and his followers. I have seen Aristotle's speech on that in the Lambda treatise, which is the end of the divine science and the limit of his philosophy, and we have discussed what he and other philosophers mentioned, and we have shown that what he said contradicts the majority of philosophers and their authorities, and he has no proof at all indicating the eternity of any part of the world; rather, his proofs indicate only the 'continuity of agency' and its consequences. And we have expanded the speech on that in the discussion on this principle and what they are confused about. And they are the innovators among the theologians who add to the Shari'a what is not indicated by a Book nor a Sunnah, nor said by any of the Salaf of the Ummah or its imams; thus they combine in their speech truth and falsehood, and the philosophers also combine truth and falsehood in their speech, and both groups do not agree with what pure reason indicates, which corresponds to what the messengers brought.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of two related claims: first, that the celestial spheres are nine in number, and second, that the world is eternal. He begins by stating that the claim of nine spheres has no proof. He then notes that most philosophers affirm the temporal origination of the world; the doctrine of eternity is uniquely associated with Aristotle and his followers. Ibn Taymiyya reports that he has examined Aristotle's arguments in the Lambda treatise (Metaphysics Book XII) and concluded that Aristotle's proofs do not establish the eternity of any part of the world; they only demonstrate the continuity of divine agency (dawam al-fa'iliyya), which is a different concept. After this, Ibn Taymiyya broadens his critique to include the innovating theologians who introduce claims into the Shari'a without evidence from Qur'an, Sunnah, or the Salaf. He characterizes both groups—philosophers and innovators—as mixing truth with falsehood, and neither conforms to pure reason that aligns with revelation. This reinforces his central thesis that sound reasoning and authentic revelation are in harmony.

Key Terms

دوام الفاعلية
المبتدعون
العقل الصريح

Ibn Taymiyya on the Fallacy of Celestial Causation
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the speculative nature of claims about the world's remaining time and the flawed assumption that all events are caused by celestial motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the underlying causal assumption that Ibn Taymiyya criticizes as corrupt in the duration claims of the world.

Core Idea
Not all events have celestial causes: Ibn Taymiyya exposes a baseless causal principle.

Ibn Taymiyya here reveals how philosophers and astronomers, lacking certain knowledge of the unseen, built speculative calculations of the world's remaining time on an unproven premise: that all events are caused by celestial motions. By exposing the dispute over astronomical data and the corrupt principle behind it, he shows that their conclusions are nothing but 'statement without knowledge.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the speculative duration claims
Locate the various numbers given for the world's remaining time (e.g., 12,000 years, 36,000 years, etc.). Notice that Ibn Taymiyya labels them as 'statement without knowledge.'
2
Find the causal principle behind them
Ibn Taymiyya states that the reason for these claims is that they knew no cause for events except the movement of the sphere. Identify this as the 'original' corrupt principle (الأصل الفاسد).
3
Examine the astronomical data used
Observe how Ibn Taymiyya presents two conflicting observations: the ancient one (1 degree per 100 years) and the later one (1 degree per 66.66 years). He argues the first is correct, but even so, the resulting durations (36,000 or 24,000 years) are only speculative.
The data is merely illustrative; the real problem is the causal assumption.
4
Recognize the logical flaw
Understand that even if the astronomical data were accurate, the whole calculation is baseless because it rests on the unproven claim that celestial motions cause all events. Without that principle, the durations have no foundation.
Ibn Taymiyya does not need to disprove the astronomy; he only needs to show the argument's dependence on an unsupported axiom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلافهم في مدة بقاء العالم بلا علم
ثم الجمهور منهم القائلون بحدوث هذا العالم تكلّم منهم طوائفُ في بقائه وفي وقت فنائه من الروم، والهند ،وغيرهم لكن بلا دليل صحيح. وسبب ذلك أنهم لم يعرفوا للحوادث التي في هذا العالم سبباً إلا حركة الفلك، وما يتجدد فيه من الأشكال، واتصالات الكواكب، فقاسوا بقاءه على ذلك فمنهم من قال: يبقى اثني عشر ألف سنة ؛ ومنهم من قال : ستة وثلاثين ألف سنة ؛ ومنهم من قال : ثلاث مئة ألف ألف سنة ؛ ومنهم من قال ثمانية وأربعين ألف سنة أو أربعة وعشرين ألف سنة . وكل ذلك قول بلا علم .
فإن منشأ النزاع أن الثوابت كان المعروفُ عندهم أنها تقطع الفلك كل مئة سنة درجة من درجات الفلك - التي هي ثلاث مئة وستون درجة. فلما رصدوها زمن المأمون زعموا أن الصحيح أنها تقطعها في ثلثي هذه المدة ـ كل ستة وستين سنة وثُلتَي سنة. والصواب أن الرصد الأول هو الصحيح. وقد اعتبر ذلك بمواضع الكواكب التي ذكرها غير واحد من القدماء في كتبهم وأصطرلاباتهم ومواضعها الآن، فدل اعتبار ذلك على أن الرصد القديم هو الصحيح، وأنها تقطع الدرجة في مئة سنة .
فإذا ضُرب ذلك في ثلاث مئة وستين كان على القول الأول ستة وثلاثين ألفاً، وعلى القول الثاني أربعة وعشرين ألفاً. ومن قال ثلاث مئة ألف وستون (ألفا) قال : هذا دَوْر في عشرة أدوار . ومن قال اثنا . ومن قال اثنا عشر ألف سنة جعل لكل برج ألف سنة. وليس معهم دليل يدل على أن هذه المدة هي مدة بقاء الفلك . والأصل الذي بنوا عليه فاسد وهو ظنهم أن الحوادث جميعها سببها حركات الفلك
Their disagreement about the duration of the world's remaining without knowledge. Then the majority of them who say that this world is temporally originated—groups among them spoke about its remaining and the time of its annihilation from the Romans, Indians, and others, but without sound proof. The reason for that is that they knew no cause for the events in this world except the movement of the sphere and what renews in it of configurations and conjunctions of planets, so they compared its remaining to that. Among them are those who said: it will remain twelve thousand years; among them are those who said: thirty-six thousand years; among them are those who said: three hundred thousand thousand years; among them are those who said: forty-eight thousand years or twenty-four thousand years. All of that is a statement without knowledge. For the origin of the dispute is that the fixed stars were known to them to traverse the sphere every hundred years one degree of the degrees of the sphere—which are three hundred and sixty degrees. When they observed them in the time of al-Ma'mun, they claimed that the correct [motion] is that they traverse it in two-thirds of this period—every sixty-six years and two-thirds of a year. But the correct [view] is that the first observation is correct. That has been verified by the positions of the planets which many of the ancients mentioned in their books and astrolabes and their positions now, and verification of that indicated that the ancient observation is correct, and that they traverse the degree in one hundred years. Then if that is multiplied by three hundred and sixty, according to the first statement it would be thirty-six thousand, and according to the second statement it would be twenty-four thousand. And whoever said three hundred thousand sixty thousand [?] said: this is a cycle of ten cycles. And whoever said twelve [thousand] [?]. And whoever said twelve thousand years made for each zodiacal sign a thousand years. They have no proof indicating that this period is the duration of the sphere's remaining. The principle upon which they built is corrupt, and it is their assumption that all events are caused by the movements of the sphere.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis by Ibn Taymiyya of the baseless claims made by some philosophers and astronomers about the duration of the world after its creation. He begins by noting that even among those who affirm the temporal origination of the world, there is disagreement about how long it will last, with various figures proposed (12,000 years, 36,000 years, etc.), all without sound evidence. The root of this confusion, he explains, is their belief that all events are caused by the movements of the celestial sphere, particularly the precession of the fixed stars. Ibn Taymiyya then recounts the astronomical data: the fixed stars were thought to move one degree every 100 years, but later observations during the caliph al-Ma'mun's time suggested a rate of one degree per 66.66 years. He argues that the older observation is correct, and that multiplying the degrees of the sphere (360) by the rate yields either 36,000 or 24,000 years, which are the figures some gave for the world's duration. However, he vehemently rejects the underlying assumption that celestial motions are the cause of all events, calling it corrupt. Thus, all such calculations are speculative and not based on certain knowledge. This critique reinforces the Islamic principle that knowledge of the unseen, such as the precise duration of the world, belongs to Allah alone.

Key Terms
الثوابت (al-thawabit) – fixed stars
الرصد (al-rasd) – astronomical observation
درجة (daraja) – degree of arc
الأصل (al-asl) – foundational assumption, here the corrupt causal principle

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The fixed stars move one degree every 100 years.
B) The world will last exactly 36,000 years.
C) All events are caused by the movements of the celestial sphere.
D) The observations of al-Ma'mun are correct.

Key Takeaway
The duration of the world is known only to Allah; speculative claims based on celestial motion are baseless because their causal principle is corrupt.

Identifying the Corrupt Foundation in Astrological Claims
Ibn Taymiyya refutes astrologers' precession claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the underlying assumption (asl) in an astrological claim and evaluate its validity using Ibn Taymiyya's method.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya refutes astrologers by exposing their unproven assumption, not by disputing astronomical data.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes on astrologers who claim to compute the precession of the fixed stars and derive cosmic cycles from it. He demonstrates that their conclusions are built on a corrupt principle: that all earthly events are caused by celestial motions. By seeing how he dissects their argument, you will learn a powerful critical tool for evaluating any claim in the Islamic sciences: always check the foundational assumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
Ibn Taymiyya presents two astrological opinions about how many years it takes for the fixed stars to traverse one degree: 66 2/3 years and 100 years. He then decides which is correct based on ancient observations.
Notice he does not dismiss astronomy itself—he uses empirical verification.
2
Trace the evidence used
He cites the positions of planets recorded by ancients and compares them with current positions. This shows that the ancient observation (100 years per degree) is correct.
He uses the method of raṣd (observation) to settle the factual dispute.
3
Extrapolate to the full cycle
He multiplies the rate by 360 degrees to get total cycle lengths: 36,000 years for the first opinion, 24,000 for the second, and others claim 360,000 or 12,000 years.
4
Identify the foundational assumption
Ibn Taymiyya states: 'The principle upon which they built is corrupt, namely their assumption that all events are caused by the movements of the celestial sphere.' This is the real target of his refutation.
He does not deny that the stars move; he denies that such motions cause earthly events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفاة الأسباب والقوى
زعموا أن الصحيح أنها تقطعها في ثلثي هذه المدة ـ كل ستة وستين سنة وثُلَتَي سنة. والصواب أن الرصد الأول هو الصحيح. وقد اعتبر ذلك بمواضع الكواكب التي ذكرها غير واحد من القدماء في كتبهم وأصطرلاباتهم ومواضعها الآن، فدل اعتبار ذلك على أن الرصد القديم هو الصحيح، وأنها تقطع الدرجة في مئة سنة .
فإذا ضرب ذلك في ثلاث مئة وستين كان على القول الأول ستة وثلاثين ألفاً، وعلى القول الثاني أربعة وعشرين ألفاً. ومن قال ثلاث مئة ألف وستون (ألفا) قال : هذا دَوْر في عشرة أدوار . ومن قال اثنا . ومن قال اثنا عشر ألف سنة جعل لكل برج ألف سنة. وليس معهم دليل يدل على . أن هذه المدة هي مدة بقاء الفلك . والأصل الذي بنوا عليه فاسد وهو ظنهم أن الحوادث جميعها سببها حركات الفلك
The deniers of causes and powers. They claimed that the correct [view] is that they [the fixed stars] traverse it in two-thirds of this period — every sixty-six years and two-thirds of a year. The correct [view] is that the first observation is correct. This has been verified by the positions of the planets mentioned by more than one of the ancients in their books and astrolabes, and their positions now. So verification indicated that the ancient observation is correct, and that they traverse a degree in one hundred years. Then if that is multiplied by three hundred and sixty, according to the first opinion it would be thirty-six thousand, and according to the second opinion twenty-four thousand. And whoever said three hundred and sixty thousand said: this is a cycle in ten cycles. And whoever said twelve... And whoever said twelve thousand years made each zodiac sign [correspond to] a thousand years. They have no proof indicating that this period is the duration of the survival of the celestial sphere. The principle upon which they built is corrupt, namely their assumption that all events are caused by the movements of the celestial sphere.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of astrologers' claims about the precession of the fixed stars. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating the two conflicting opinions: some claim the fixed stars traverse a degree in 66 2/3 years, others in 100 years. He asserts that the correct view is the ancient observation, which is supported by comparing the positions of stars recorded by ancients with their current positions. This establishes that the precession is 100 years per degree. He then works out the total period for a full cycle (360 degrees) under each opinion, showing that some claim a cycle of 36,000 years, others 24,000, etc. But he dismisses all these because they lack proof that such a period corresponds to the life of the celestial sphere. The real issue is the corrupt foundation: the assumption that all events are caused by the movements of the heavens. By pointing out the lack of evidence and the flawed principle, Ibn Taymiyya undermines the entire astrological enterprise.

رصد
درجة
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The assumption that the fixed stars move at a constant speed.

D) The assumption that the celestial sphere has a finite lifetime.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya teaches that a claim's foundation must be examined: if it rests on an unproven causal assumption, the entire argument collapses.

The Ash'ari Denial of Causality
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the Mutakallimun who deny all causal efficacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the Ash'ari doctrine of 'fa‘ala ‘indahu lā bihi' and identify Ibn Taymiyya's main criticisms.

Core Idea
Denying all causes contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and reason.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya confronts the theologians who deny any causal efficacy in creation. They claim that God acts 'at it not by it'—meaning creatures have no real power. Ibn Taymiyya counters that this position opposes the fundamental sources of Islam. Let's examine how he frames his critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari position
Locate the claim that creatures have no causal efficacy: 'ليس لشيء من حركات الفلك تأثير' and the formula 'فَعَل عنده لا به.'
2
List Ibn Taymiyya's four sources of refutation
He says this position opposes the Book, Sunnah, consensus of the Salaf, and clear intellects.
These are the authorities he appeals to.
3
Explain the formula 'fa‘ala ‘indahu lā bihi'
This means God creates the act accompanying the creature's act, not through its power. Contrast this with affirming real causation.
This is a key Ash'ari doctrine.
4
Assess the seriousness of the critique
Ibn Taymiyya declares that the denial of causes contradicts the foundational sources of Islam, making it a grave error.
He does not yet provide evidence here; that comes in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الأصل، قد تقابلوا فيه هم والمبتدعة من أهل الكلام. فأولئك يقولون: ليس لشيء من حركات الفلك تأثير في هذا العالم، ولا شيء منها سبب في حدوث شيء . يطردون هذا في جميع الموجودات، فلا يجعلون الله خَلَق شيئاً بسبب، ولا لحكمة. ولا يجعلون للإنسان قدرةً تؤثر في مقدورها، ولا لشيء من الأجسام طبيعة، ولا غريزة. بل يقولون : فَعَل عنده لا به. وخالفوا بذلك الكتاب والسنة ، وإجماع السلف والأئمة، وصرائح العقول.

المقام الرابع - مقابلة المتكلمين النفاة للأسباب والقوى للفلاسفة

فإن الله تعالى يقول: ﴿إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي الباء السببية في القرآن تجرى في البَحْرِ بِمَا يَنفَعُ النَّاسَ وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن ماءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كلِ دَابَةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الحَ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخَّرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ ) [سورة البقرة : ١٦٤]، وقال: ﴿ وَهُوَ الَّذِى يُرْسِلُ الرِّيحَ بُشْرًا بَيْنَ يَدَى رَحْمَتِهِ حَتَّى إِذَا أَقلَتْ سَحَابًا ثِقَالًا سُقْنَهُ لِبَلَدِ مَيْت فَأَنزَلْنَا بِهِ الْمَاء فَأَخَرَجْنَا بِهِ مِن كُلِّ الثَّمَرَاتِ كَذَلِكَ تُخْرِجُ الْمَوْلَى لَعَلَّكُمْ تَذَكَّرُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأعراف : ٥٧]، وقال: ﴿ وَنَزَّلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً مُبَرَكَا فَأَنْبَتْنَا بِهِ جَنَّاتٍ وَحَبَّ الْحَصِيدِ ﴾ [سورة ق : ۹] . ومثل هذا كثير في الكتاب والسنة . يذكر سبحانه أنه فعل هذا بهذا ، كما ذكر أنه أنزل الماء بالسحاب، وأنه أحيا الأرض بالماء.

والعلماء متفقون على إثبات حكمة الله في خلقه وأمره ، وإثبات الأسباب والقوى، كما قد ذكرنا أقوالهم في مواضعها . وليس من السلف من أنكر كون حركات الكواكب قد تكون من تمام أسباب الحوادث كما أن الله جعل هبوب الرياح ونور الشمس والقمر من أسباب الحوادث .

وقد ثبت في الصحيحين عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : «إن الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله ، لا تنكسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته، ولكنهما آيتان من آيات الله يخوف الله بهما عباده. فإذ رأيتموهما فافْزَعُوا إلى الصلاة» . وأمر عند الكسوف بالصلاة ،والذكر والدعاء، والصدقة والعِتاقة والاستغفار. وكذلك عند سائر الآيات التي يخوف الله بها عباده .
And this principle, they and the innovators among the theologians have opposed each other regarding it. Those [theologians] say: There is no effect for any of the movements of the celestial sphere in this world, nor is any of them a cause for the occurrence of anything. They generalize this to all existents, so they do not make God create anything by a cause, nor for wisdom. They do not affirm for man any power that influences its object, nor for any body a nature or an instinct. Rather they say: He acts at it not by it. By this, they oppose the Book, the Sunnah, the consensus of the Salaf and the Imams, and clear intellects.

The Fourth Station - Confronting the Theologians who Deny Causes and Powers, [in opposition] to the Philosophers.

For indeed Allah the Exalted says: 'Indeed in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships which sail through the sea with that which benefits people, and what Allah has sent down from the sky of water and given life thereby to the earth after its death and dispersed therein every creature, and the directing of the winds and the clouds controlled between the heaven and the earth are signs for a people who reason' [Surah Al-Baqarah: 164]. And He said: 'And it is He who sends the winds as good tidings before His mercy until, when they have gathered heavy clouds, We drive them to a dead land and send down thereby water and bring forth thereby fruit of every kind. Thus will We bring forth the dead; perhaps you may remember' [Surah Al-A'raf: 57]. And He said: 'And We sent down from the sky blessed water and caused to grow thereby gardens and grain of the harvest' [Surah Qaf: 9]. And similar to this is abundant in the Book and the Sunnah. He mentions that He did this by means of this, just as He mentioned that He sent down water by the clouds, and that He gave life to the earth by water.

And the scholars are agreed on affirming the wisdom of Allah in His creation and His command, and affirming causes and powers, as we have mentioned their statements in their places. And there is none among the Salaf who denied that the movements of the planets may be part of the complete causes of events, just as Allah made the blowing of winds and the light of the sun and moon among the causes of events.

And it is established in the two Sahihs from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Indeed the sun and the moon are two signs from the signs of Allah; they do not eclipse for the death of anyone nor for his life, but they are two signs from the signs of Allah by which He frightens His servants. So when you see them, hasten to prayer.' And he commanded at the eclipse: prayer, remembrance, supplication, charity, freeing slaves, and seeking forgiveness. And likewise for all [other] signs by which Allah frightens His servants.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the theological position (mainly associated with the Ash'ari mutakallimun) that denies any causal efficacy in created things. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that these theologians deny any effect of celestial movements and generalize this denial to all existents: they deny that God creates anything for a cause or wisdom, deny human power, deny natures and instincts in bodies, and instead assert that God acts 'at it not by it' (i.e., alongside the action without causal connection). He declares that this opposes the Quran, Sunnah, consensus of the Salaf, and clear intellects. Then he introduces the fourth section heading: 'Confronting the Theologians who Deny Causes and Powers, in opposition to the Philosophers.' He proceeds to prove the reality of causation by quoting Quranic verses that use the preposition 'bi' (by means of) to indicate causation, such as God giving life to the earth by water, sending rain by clouds, etc. He notes that such expressions are abundant. Then he states that the scholars (the Salaf) are unanimous in affirming God's wisdom and causes and powers, and that none of the Salaf denied that planetary movements can be among the complete causes of events. He supports this with the prophetic hadith about eclipses, where the Prophet commanded prayer, charity, etc., during eclipses, showing that these events have causes and purposes. Thus, Ibn Taymiyya uses both textual and rational arguments to refute the complete denial of causality.

Key Terms
فعل عنده لا به

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main criticism Ibn Taymiyya levels against the theologians who deny causes?
A) They contradict the Quran and Sunnah
B) They ignore philosophy
C) They deny God's power
D) They are influenced by Greek thought

Key Takeaway
Denying all causal efficacy contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, consensus of the Salaf, and clear reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the Ash'ari formula 'فعل عنده لا به' and explain why Ibn Taymiyya rejects it using the four sources he mentions (Book, Sunnah, consensus, intellect).

Quranic and Sunnah Evidence for Causal Efficacy
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the Mutakallimun who deny all causal efficacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze Quranic verses and prophetic hadith to demonstrate that causation is affirmed in Islamic sources.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah repeatedly attribute effects to natural means as instruments of God.

Ibn Taymiyya now moves from accusation to proof. He cites several Quranic verses that use the preposition 'bi' (by means of) to indicate causation: God gives life to the earth by water, sends rain by clouds, etc. He also invokes the Prophetic hadith on solar eclipses to show that events have purposes. Let's examine how these texts establish the reality of causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses
Find the three verses cited: Baqarah 164, A'raf 57, Qaf 9. Note the repeated structure 'bi' indicating means.
The preposition 'bi' is the key linguistic indicator.
2
Extract the causal construction
In each verse, God attributes an effect to a means: 'أَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ' (gave life to the earth by it), 'فَأَنزَلْنَا بِهِ الْمَاءَ' (sent down water by it), 'فَأَنْبَتْنَا بِهِ جَنَّاتٍ' (caused gardens to grow by it).
The means (water, clouds) are instrumental, not independent.
3
Connect the means to the effect
Recognize that God attributes the effect to the means without compromising His sovereignty. This shows secondary causation is real.
Ibn Taymiyya uses this to counter the claim that God acts 'at it not by it.'
4
Analyze the prophetic hadith
The hadith about eclipses instructs prayer, charity, etc. This shows eclipses have a purpose (a sign from God), implying they are caused events, not merely arbitrary.
This further supports the reality of causes and purposes.

Source Text

And this principle, they and the innovators among the theologians have opposed each other regarding it. Those [theologians] say: There is no effect for any of the movements of the celestial sphere in this world, nor is any of them a cause for the occurrence of anything. They generalize this to all existents, so they do not make God create anything by a cause, nor for wisdom. They do not affirm for man any power that influences its object, nor for any body a nature or an instinct. Rather they say: He acts at it not by it. The Fourth Station - Confronting the Theologians who Deny Causes and Powers, [in opposition] to the Philosophers.

For indeed Allah the Exalted says: 'Indeed in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships which sail through the sea with that which benefits people, and what Allah has sent down from the sky of water and given life thereby to the earth after its death and dispersed therein every creature, and the directing of the winds and the clouds controlled between the heaven and the earth are signs for a people who reason' [Surah Al-Baqarah: 164]. And He said: 'And it is He who sends the winds as good tidings before His mercy until, when they have gathered heavy clouds, We drive them to a dead land and send down thereby water and bring forth thereby fruit of every kind. Thus will We bring forth the dead; perhaps you may remember' [Surah Al-A'raf: 57]. And He said: 'And We sent down from the sky blessed water and caused to grow thereby gardens and grain of the harvest' [Surah Qaf: 9]. And similar to this is abundant in the Book and the Sunnah. He mentions that He did this by means of this, just as He mentioned that He sent down water by the clouds, and that He gave life to the earth by water.

And the scholars are agreed on affirming the wisdom of Allah in His creation and His command, and affirming causes and powers, as we have mentioned their statements in their places. And there is none among the Salaf who denied that the movements of the planets may be part of the complete causes of events, just as Allah made the blowing of winds and the light of the sun and moon among the causes of events.

And it is established in the two Sahihs from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Indeed the sun and the moon are two signs from the signs of Allah; they do not eclipse for the death of anyone nor for his life, but they are two signs from the signs of Allah by which He frightens His servants. So when you see them, hasten to prayer.' And he commanded at the eclipse: prayer, remembrance, supplication, charity, freeing slaves, and seeking forgiveness. And likewise for all [other] signs by which Allah frightens His servants.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the theological position (mainly associated with the Ash'ari mutakallimun) that denies any causal efficacy in created things. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that these theologians deny any effect of celestial movements and generalize this denial to all existents: they deny that God creates anything for a cause or wisdom, deny human power, deny natures and instincts in bodies, and instead assert that God acts 'at it not by it' (i.e., alongside the action without causal connection). He declares that this opposes the Quran, Sunnah, consensus of the Salaf, and clear intellects. Thus, Ibn Taymiyya uses both textual and rational arguments to refute the complete denial of causality.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Occasionalist Denial of Causes
Ibn Taymiyya attacks occasionalist denial of causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's main arguments against occasionalist denial of causality and assess their basis in revelation and consensus.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya insists that God's actions through means (causes) is proven by the Quran, consensus, and reason.

In this passage from his refutation, Ibn Taymiyya confronts the occasionalist theologians who claim that God does not create through any means or causes. He argues that their position contradicts the explicit language of the Quran, the consensus of the Salaf, and clear rational principles. We will examine his critique and how he uses Quranic verses to establish instrumental causality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occasionalist position
Read the first paragraph and locate the phrase 'فعل عنده لا به'. This captures the essence of occasionalism: God acts concurrently with events, not through them.
This phrase is key.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's grounds for rejection
He claims the position contradicts the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and reason. Look for these four pillars.
He provides evidence for each.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
He cites three verses where God uses the preposition 'bi' to indicate instrumentality. Identify the word 'به' in each verse.
e.g., فأحيا به الأرض
4
Assess the appeal to consensus
He asserts that the scholars and Salaf unanimously affirm causes. Consider whether his claim is supported by the examples he provides.
He mentions earlier discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - مقابلة المتكلمين النفاة للأسباب والقوى للفلاسفة
لشيء من حركات الفلك تأثير في هذا العالم، ولا شيء منها سبب في حدوث شيء. بل يطردون هذا في جميع الموجودات، فلا يجعلون الله خَلَق شيئاً بسبب، ولا لحكمة. ولا يجعلون للإنسان قدرةً تؤثر في مقدورها، ولا لشيء من الأجسام طبيعة، ولا غريزة. بل يقولون : فَعَل عنده لا به. وخالفوا بذلك الكتاب والسنة، وإجماع السلف والأئمة، وصرائح العقول.
فإن الله تعالى يقول: ﴿إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الْيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِمَا يَنفَعُ النَّاسَ وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن ماءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ دَابَّةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّيَاحِ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخَّرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [سورة البقرة : ١٦٤]، وقال: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي يُرْسِلُ الرِّيَاحَ بُشْرًا بَيْنَ يَدَيْ رَحْمَتِهِ حَتَّى إِذَا أَقَلَّتْ سَحَابًا ثِقَالًا سُقْنَهُ لِبَلَدٍ مَيِّتٍ فَأَنزَلْنَا بِهِ الْمَاءَ فَأَخْرَجْنَا بِهِ مِن كُلِّ الثَّمَرَاتِ كَذَلِكَ نُخْرِجُ الْمَوْتَى لَعَلَّكُمْ تَذَكَّرُونَ﴾ [سورة الأعراف : ٥٧]، وقال: ﴿وَنَزَّلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً مُبَارَكًا فَأَنبَتْنَا بِهِ جَنَّاتٍ وَحَبَّ الْحَصِيدِ﴾ [سورة ق : ٩] . ومثل هذا كثير في الكتاب والسنة . يذكر سبحانه أنه فعل هذا بهذا، كما ذكر أنه أنزل الماء بالسحاب، وأنه أحيا الأرض بالماء.
والعلماء متفقون على إثبات حكمة الله في خلقه وأمره، وإثبات الأسباب والقوى، كما قد ذكرنا أقوالهم في مواضعها . وليس من السلف من أنكر كون حركات الكواكب قد تكون من تمام أسباب الحوادث كما أن الله جعل هبوب الرياح ونور الشمس والقمر من أسباب الحوادث .
وقد ثبت في الصحيحين عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : «إن الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله، لا تنكسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته، ولكنهما آيتان من آيات الله يخوف الله بهما عباده. فإذا رأيتموهما فافزعوا إلى الصلاة» . وأَمر عند الكسوف بالصلاة، والذكر والدعاء، والصدقة والعتاقة والاستغفار. وكذلك عند سائر الآيات التي يخوف الله بها عباده .
وقوله : «لا تنكسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته» رد لما كان قد توهمه بعض الناس من أن كسوف الشمس كان لأجل موت إبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وكان قد مات وكسفت الشمس، فتوهم بعضُ الجهال من المسلمين أن الكسوف كان لأجل هذا . فبين لهم النبي أن الكسوف لا يكون سببه موتُ أحد من أهل الأرض، ونفى بذلك أن يكون الكسوف معلولاً عن ذلك. وظنوا أن هذا من جنس اهتزاز العرش لموت سعد بن معاذ، كما ثبت ذلك في الصحيح . فنفى النبيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ذلك، وبين أن ذلك من آيات الله التي يخوف بها عباده . والتخويف إنما يكون بما يكون سبباً للشر. قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا نُرْسِلُ بِالْآيَاتِ إِلَّا تَخْوِيفًا﴾ [سورة الإسراء : ٥٩]. فلو كان الكسوف وجوده كعدمه بالنسبة إلى الحوادث لم يكن سبباً لشر، وهو خلاف نص الرسول .
وأيضاً في السنن أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نظر إلى القمر وقال لعائشة : يا عائشة! تعوّذي بالله من شر هذا، فإن هذا هو الغاسِقُ إِذَا وَقَبَ . والاستعاذة إنما تكون مما يحدث عنه شرّ .
وأمر صلى الله عليه وسلم عند انعقاد أسباب الشر بما يدفع مُوجِبَها بمشيئة الله تعالى وقدرته من الصلاة والدعاء، والذكر والاستغفار والتوبة والإحسان بالصدقة والعتاقة. فإن هذه الأعمال الصالحة تعارض الشرَّ الذي انعقد سببه، كما في الحديث : «إن الدعاء والبلاء ليلتقيان بين السماء والأرض، فيَعْتَلِجان» .
The Fourth Station - Confronting the Theologians who Deny Causes and Powers to the Philosophers: Nothing from the movements of the celestial sphere has any effect in this world, and nothing from them is a cause for the occurrence of anything. Rather, they apply this to all existents, so they do not make God create anything by a cause, nor for wisdom. And they do not make for man a power that affects its object of power, nor for any body a nature, nor an instinct. Rather, they say: He acts at (the time of) it, not by it. And by that they have contradicted the Book, the Sunnah, the consensus of the Salaf and the Imams, and the clear dictates of intellects. For God Almighty says: “Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships which sail through the sea with that which benefits people, and what God has sent down from the sky of water, and revives thereby the earth after its death and disperses therein every [kind of] creature, and [His] directing of the winds and the clouds controlled between the heaven and the earth are signs for a people who use reason” [Surah al-Baqarah: 164], and He said: “And it is He who sends the winds as good tidings before His mercy until, when they have carried heavy clouds, We drive them to a dead land and send down thereby rain and bring forth thereby from all the fruits. Thus will We bring forth the dead; perhaps you may be reminded” [Surah al-A'raf: 57], and He said: “And We have sent down from the sky blessed rain and caused to grow thereby gardens and grain of the harvest” [Surah Qaf: 9]. And similar to this is much in the Book and the Sunnah. He mentions that He does this by means of that, just as He mentioned that He sends down rain by clouds, and that He revives the earth by water. And the scholars are unanimous upon affirming the wisdom of God in His creation and command, and affirming causes and powers, as we have mentioned their statements in their places. And there is none of the Salaf who denied that the movements of the celestial bodies may be among the complete causes of events, just as God made the blowing of winds and the light of the sun and moon from the causes of events. And it is established in the two Sahihs from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: “Indeed, the sun and the moon are two signs among the signs of God. They do not eclipse for the death of anyone nor for his life, but they are two signs from the signs of God by which God frightens His servants. So when you see them, hasten to prayer.” And he commanded at eclipse with prayer, remembrance, supplication, charity, emancipation, and seeking forgiveness. And likewise for the rest of the signs by which God frightens His servants. And his saying: “They do not eclipse for the death of anyone nor for his life” is a refutation of what some people had supposed that the eclipse of the sun was due to the death of Ibrahim, the son of the Prophet, peace be upon him. He had died and the sun eclipsed, so some ignorant among the Muslims supposed that the eclipse was because of that. So the Prophet explained to them that the eclipse is not caused by the death of anyone from the people of the earth, and he thereby negated that the eclipse is an effect of that. And they thought that this is of the kind of the shaking of the Throne at the death of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, as is established in the Sahih. So the Prophet negated that and explained that this is among the signs of God by which He frightens His servants. And frightening is only by what is a cause of evil. God Almighty said: “And We do not send the signs except as a fright” [Surah al-Isra: 59]. So if the eclipse were like its non-existence with respect to events, it would not be a cause of evil, and that is contrary to the text of the Messenger. And also in the Sunan that the Prophet looked at the moon and said to Aisha: O Aisha! Seek refuge with Allah from the evil of this, for this is the darkening one when it covers. And seeking refuge is only from what would cause evil. And he commanded, peace be upon him, at the conjunction of the causes of evil with what repels its necessitator by the will of God Almighty and His power, from prayer, supplication, remembrance, seeking forgiveness, repentance, and benevolence with charity and emancipation. For these righteous deeds counteract the evil whose cause has been set, as in the hadith: “Supplication and affliction meet between heaven and earth and wrestle.”
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the occasionalist theologians (mutakallimun) who deny causality—that is, they deny that any created thing has a real causal power or that God creates through means. Ibn Taymiyya begins by describing their position: they deny that celestial movements have any effect in this world, that anything is a cause of another, and they extend this denial to all existents. According to them, God does not create anything by a cause or for a purpose; humans have no effective power; bodies have no natures or instincts. Rather, they say God acts 'at the thing' but not 'by it' (فَعَل عنده لا به)—meaning God creates events concurrently with the occasion, not through any causal efficacy of the occasion. This, Ibn Taymiyya insists, contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, consensus of the Salaf and the Imams, and clear reason. He then provides Quranic evidence: Surah al-Baqarah 2:164, where God mentions reviving the earth 'by' water (فأحيا به الأرض), and Surah al-A'raf 7:57, where God sends wind, then drives clouds, then sends down rain, and brings forth fruits 'by it'. The repeated preposition 'ب' (bi) indicates that the water is instrumental: God brings about life by means of water. These verses show that God's actions are through causes. He then cites Surah Qaf 50:9 similarly. He argues that the scholars unanimously affirm God's wisdom and causality, and that no early Muslim (Salaf) denied that celestial motions may be among the complete causes of events—just as wind and sunlight are causes. He then turns to the Prophetic hadith on eclipses: the sun and moon are signs of God; they do not eclipse for anyone's death or life. The Prophet negated that eclipses are caused by human events, but this does not negate causality itself. Rather, the eclipse has a causal role: it is a sign that frightens, and frightening is a cause of evil. The Prophet commanded prayer, charity, etc. at eclipses, which are acts that counteract evil. Ibn Taymiyya highlights that the Prophet also sought refuge from the 'darkening one' (الغاسق), which is the moon when eclipsed, showing that the eclipse itself is a cause of evil (since one seeks refuge from evil things). He concludes that the command to seek refuge and perform good deeds shows that the eclipse is a real cause of evil, contradicting the occasionalist view that it has no effect. The entire argument is a systematic defense of causality from revelation and reason.
