Philosophical Ta'wil: The Batini Reinterpretation of Qur'anic Symbols
Ibn Taymiyya traces Batini origins and their philosophical corruption of Islamic doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the philosophical reinterpretations of al-lawḥ, al-qalam, and other Qur'anic terms as reported by Ibn Taymiyya, and evaluate the epistemological implications of the philosophers' approach to bodily resurrection.

Core Idea
The philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection reveals that their ta'wil treats prophetic statements as useful fictions for the masses.

In this lesson, we delve into how Ibn Taymiyya exposes the philosophical corruption of specific Qur'anic symbols by the Batinis and their philosopher allies. You will learn to recognize the esoteric identifications and understand why Ibn Taymiyya considers the philosophers' stance on bodily resurrection a devastating indictment of their entire approach.

Guided Path
1
List the philosophical identifications
Ibn Taymiyya reports that the Batinis said the Tablet is the Universal Soul, the Pen is the Active Intellect, and the celestial bodies seen by Abraham are the Soul, Active Intellect, and First Intellect. Find these in the text.
These are clear cases of ta'wil (esoteric interpretation).
2
Contrast with orthodox understanding
In orthodox Islam, the Tablet and Pen are created entities that record destinies. Note how the philosophical interpretation replaces them with emanations in a Neoplatonic scheme.
This shows the substitution of revelation with philosophy.
3
Explain the stance on attributes and resurrection
Ibn Taymiyya says the verifiers among the philosophers (like Ibn Sina) claim that attributes and bodily resurrection are not to be interpreted; they are merely rhetorical tools for the masses. Find the sentence that says they are 'not established in reality'.
This is a key point: they deny any real truth to these doctrines.
4
Analyze the implication
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that this view entails that the prophets lied for the benefit of the public. Trace his reasoning: if the prophetic statements are not true in reality, then they must be falsehoods.
This is a logical consequence of their position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - تاريخ الباطنية وأحوالهم. وأما قرامطة البحرين أبو سعيد بن الجنابي وأصحابه، فأولئك كانوا يتظاهرون بالكفر الصريح. ولهذا قتلوا الحجاج، وألقوهم في بئر زمزم، وأخذوا الحجر الأسود، وبقي عندهم مدة بخلاف العبيديين، فإنهم كانوا يتظاهرون بالإسلام، ويقولون إنهم شيعة. فالظاهر عنهم الرفض، لكن كان باطنهم الإلحاد والزندقة، كما قال أبو حامد الغزالي في كتاب «المستظهري»: «ظاهرهم الرفض، وباطنهم الكفر المحض». وهذا الذي قاله أبو حامد فيهم هو متفق عليه بين علماء المسلمين. وكانوا يأمرون عامتهم بالعبادات، وهم على درجات مرتبة عندهم كلما ارتفع درجة غيروا الشريعة عنده، فإذا انتهى، أسقطوا عنه الشرائع. وكان ابن الصباح من أتباعهم أخذ عن المستنصر الذي جرى في أيامه فتنة البساسيري. وهو الذي أحدث السكين وأصحاب الألموت من أتباعه. والذين كانوا بالشام كسنان ونحوه هم من أتباع أولئك وباطنهم مركب من مذهب المجوس والفلاسفة. أخذوا عن المجوس الأصلين: النور والظلمة، وأخذوا عن الفلاسفة العقل والنفس، وعبروا هم عن ذلك بـ «السابق» و «التالي». فلما دخل معهم المتفلسفة كابن سينا وأمثاله تبين لهم أن ما يدعونه على الرسول من التأويلات مما يعلم بطلان كثير منها بالضرورة، والفيلسوف من حيث هو فيلسوف ليس له غرض فيما يعلم أنه باطل، فسلكوا مسلكاً بين مسلك هؤلاء الملاحدة وبين دين المسلمين. فالشرائع الظاهرة أقروها ولم يتأولوها، لكن قد يقولون: إن بعضها يسقط الخاصة. ودخل معهم في هذا طائفة من متصوفة الفلاسفة كابن عربي وابن سبعين وغيرهما. وأما العلميات فتأولوا بعضها، كاللوح، قالوا: هو النفس الكلية؛ والقلم، قالوا: العقل الفعال؛ وربما قالوا عن الكوكب، والشمس والقمر، التي رآها إبراهيم: إنها النفس، والعقل الفعال، والعقل الأول؛ وتأولوا الملائكة، ونحو ذلك. وأما صفات الرب، ومعاد الأبدان، وغير ذلك، فمذهب محققيهم كابن سينا وأمثاله أنها لا تتأول، وأن ما دلت عليه ليس ثابتاً في نفس الأمر، ولا يستفاد منها علم. قالوا: بل المراد منها خطاب الجمهور بما يخيل إليهم ما يعتقدونه في أمر الإيمان بالله واليوم الآخر لينتفعوا بذلك الاعتقاد، وإن كان باطلاً لا حقيقة له في نفس الأمر. فإن هذا غايته أن الأنبياء كذبوا لمصلحة الجمهور وهم يرون مثل ذلك من تمام حكمتهم. والمعاد للأبدان.
The fourth station - History of the Batinis and their conditions. As for the Qaramita of Bahrain, Abu Sa'id bin al-Janabi and his companions, those used to manifest outright disbelief. For this reason they killed the pilgrims, threw them into the well of Zamzam, and took the Black Stone, and it remained with them for a period, unlike the Fatimids, for they used to manifest Islam and claim that they were Shia. So outwardly they showed Shi'ism, but their inner was atheism and heresy, as Abu Hamid al-Ghazali said in his book al-Mustazhiri: 'Their outward is Shi'ism, their inner is pure disbelief.' And what Abu Hamid said about them is agreed upon among Muslim scholars. And they used to command their commoners to perform acts of worship, while they had graded ranks; whenever one rose in rank, he altered the Sharia for them, and when he reached the end, they dropped the religious laws from him. And Ibn al-Sabbah was among their followers, receiving from al-Mustansir, in whose days occurred the fitna of al-Basasiri. It was he who introduced the dagger, and the people of Alamut were his followers. And those who were in Syria, like Sinan and the like, are followers of those, and their inner doctrine is composed of the school of the Magians and the philosophers. They took from the Magians the two principles: light and darkness, and they took from the philosophers 'the intellect' and 'the soul', and they expressed that as 'the Precedent' and 'the Consequent'. Then when the philosophizers like Ibn Sina and his likes joined them, they realized that what they claim about the Prophet of esoteric interpretations, many of which are known to be false necessarily, and the philosopher qua philosopher has no interest in what he knows is false, so they followed a middle course between the course of those heretics and the religion of the Muslims. So they affirmed the external laws and did not interpret them, but they might say that some of them are dropped for the elite. And a group of philosopher-sufis like Ibn 'Arabi and Ibn Sab'in and others joined them in this. As for the theoretical matters, they interpreted some of them, like the Tablet; they said: it is the Universal Soul; and the Pen; they said: it is the Active Intellect. And sometimes they said about the planet, the sun and the moon that Ibrahim saw: that they are the Soul, the Active Intellect, and the First Intellect. And they interpreted the angels and the like. And as for the attributes of the Lord, the resurrection of bodies, and other matters, the doctrine of their verifiers like Ibn Sina and his likes is that these are not to be interpreted, and that what they indicate is not established in reality, nor is knowledge obtained from them. They said: Rather, the intended meaning is addressing the public with what suggests to them what they believe concerning faith in God and the Last Day so that they benefit from that belief, even if it is false with no reality in truth. For at most this entails that the prophets lied for the benefit of the public, and they consider such to be part of their perfect wisdom. And the resurrection of bodies.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a historical and doctrinal critique by Ibn Taymiyya of the Batini sects and their philosophical allies. He begins by distinguishing the Qaramita of Bahrain, who openly displayed disbelief, from the Fatimids who outwardly professed Islam but were inwardly heretics, citing al-Ghazali. He then describes their graded initiation system where higher ranks abandon Sharia. Next, he turns to the Assassins (al-Sabbah, Alamut), noting their inner doctrine combines Magian dualism (light/darkness) with philosophical concepts (intellect/soul), which they call 'the Precedent' and 'the Consequent'. Ibn Taymiyya then criticizes the 'philosophizers' like Ibn Sina who, seeing the falsity of many Batini interpretations, adopted a compromise: they affirmed outward Sharia but claimed it drops for the elite. They engaged in esoteric interpretation (ta'wil) of certain religious symbols: the Tablet becomes the Universal Soul, the Pen the Active Intellect, and the celestial bodies seen by Abraham become cosmic intellects. However, regarding God's attributes and bodily resurrection, the philosophers like Ibn Sina denied any real interpretation; they claimed these doctrines are merely rhetorical devices to benefit the common people, even if false. This, Ibn Taymiyya concludes, implies that prophets lied for the public good, which he presents as a devastating critique of the philosophical approach.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what did the Batinis identify with 'al-lawḥ' and 'al-qalam'?
A) The Preserved Tablet and Pen
B) Universal soul and active intellect
C) Light and darkness
D) The precedent and consequent

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' esoteric ta'wil of bodily resurrection reduces prophetic statements to useful lies, a conclusion that Ibn Taymiyya exposes as incompatible with Islamic belief in prophetic truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In the passage, Ibn Taymiyya lists several esoteric identifications. Choose one (e.g., Tablet = Universal Soul) and explain why this substitution changes the meaning from an Islamic perspective.
?
Construct a brief logical argument (in syllogistic form) that Ibn Taymiyya could use to show that the philosophers' view on bodily resurrection implies that prophets lied.

Philosophers' Epistemological Hierarchy: Undermining Prophetic Authority
Ibn Taymiyya critiques philosophers' and heretical Sufis' views on prophecy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophical distinction between practical and theoretical prophetic knowledge, and identify its consequences for religious obligation.

Core Idea
Philosophers reduce prophecy to practical law and deny its theoretical authority.

Ibn Taymiyya exposes a dangerous intellectual trend: philosophers accept prophetic laws for social order but reject them as sources of truth about God and the afterlife. This lesson dissects his critique and its implications for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
In the passage, Ibn Taymiyya states that philosophers magnify the practical laws (al-sharā’i‘ al-‘amaliyya) but consider theoretical knowledge (al-sharā’i‘ al-‘ilmiyya) as the domain of philosophy, not prophecy. Locate the Arabic terms and understand what each covers.
Practical laws include rulings of worship and transactions; theoretical knowledge includes beliefs about God and the afterlife.
2
Examine the two factions
Some philosophers say the prophet is greater but uses imagination (takhīl) for public benefit, even if false. Others say the philosopher is greater and the prophet is only skilled in practical law. Identify each position and its implications for prophetic truthfulness.
The first faction claims prophets inwardly follow philosophy but outwardly present imaginative stories; the second claims prophets may be ignorant of deeper truths.
3
Trace the consequences
Ibn Taymiyya shows that these views lead to deeming Islam non-obligatory, allowing Jews and Christians to remain on their religions. Find the anecdote of the seeker and shaykh that illustrates this relativism.
The shaykh asks whether the seeker wants to follow Islam, Judaism, or Christianity, and says 'Muslims are better than them' rather than affirming Islam as the only truth.
4
Evaluate the historical correction
Ibn Taymiyya corrects the confusion between Alexander the Macedonian and Dhul-Qarnayn. Why does he include this? How does it reinforce his critique of the philosophers' reliability?
He distinguishes Dhul-Qarnayn as a righteous Muslim ruler, while Alexander was a polytheist, showing that philosophers like Aristotle served polytheistic rulers.

المقام الرابع - غرائب الفلاسفة
وهم يعظمون شرائعَ الأنبياء العَمَلية. وأما العِلْمية فعندهم العلم في ذلك بما يقوله الفلاسفة . وأما الأنبياء فلا يُستفاد من جهتهم علم بذلك .
ثم منهم من يقول النبي أعظم من الفيلسوف فيقولون: النبي كان في الباطن على مذهب هؤلاء الفلاسفة، لكن خاصته التخييلُ وإن كان كذباً في الحقيقة لمصلحة الجمهور. ومنهم من يقول : بل الفيلسوف أعظم من النبي، والنبي قد لا يكون عارفاً في الباطن بما يجوز على الله وما لا يجوز وحقيقة الأمر في المعاد، لكن هو حاذق في وضع الشرائع العملية .
مصنف
وكثير من ملاحدة المتصوفة كابن عربي وابن سبعين، والقُوْنَوِي، والتلمساني وغيرهم، يوافقونهم في أصولهم، لكن يغيرون العبارات فيعبّرون بالعبارات الإسلامية عما هو قولهم. وفي الكُتُب المضنون بها على غير أهلها وغيرها من كتب مصنفيها قطعة من هذا. وبسبب ذلك وقع ابن عربي وأمثاله من ملاحدة المتصوفة مع هؤلاء. ولهذا كثر كلام علماء المسلمين في مصنفيها. ومن الناس من ينكر أن تكون من كلام أبي حامد لما رأى ما فيها من المصائب العظيمة. وآخرون يقولون : بل رجع عن ذلك وخُتم له بالاشتغال بالبخاري ومسلم، كما قد ذكر ذلك في سيرته . وهؤلاء المتفلسفة ومتصوفوهم كابن سبعين وأتباعه يجوزون أن يكون الرجل يهودياً أو نصرانياً أو مشركاً يعبد الأوثان . فليس الإسلام عندهم واجباً، ولا التهود والتنصر والشرك محرّماً ، لكن قد يرجحون شريعة الإسلام على غيرها .
وإذا جاء المريدُ إلى شيخ من شيوخهم، وقال أريد أن أسلك على يديك، يقول له : على دين المسلمين، أو اليهود، أو النصارى؟» فإذا قال له المريد : «اليهود والنصارى أما هُمْ كُفَّار ؟ ) يقول : لا ، ولكن المسلمون خير منهم. وهذا من جنس جُهّال التَّتَر أَوَّلَ ما أسلموا . فإن الإسلام عندهم خير من غيره، وإن كان غيره جائزاً لا يُوالون عليه ويُعادون عليه .
وهذا أيضاً أكثر اعتقاد علماء النصارى وكثير من اليهود. يرون دين بمنزلة مذاهب المسلمين واليهود والنصارى بمنزلة المذاهب في دين المسلمين فيجوز للرجل عندهم أن ينتقل من هذه الملة إلى تلك إما لرجحانها عنده في الدين، وإما لمصلحة دنياه، كما ينتقل الإنسان من مذهب بعض أئمة المسلمين إلى مذهب آخر، كما ينتقل من مذهب مالك إلى الشافعي، ومن مذهب أبي حنيفة إلى مذهب أحمد، ونحو ذلك .
وأما أرسطو وأصحابه فكانوا مشركين يعبدون الأصنام والكواكب. وهكذا كان دين اليونان والروم قبل ظهور دين المسيح فيهم. وكان أرسطو قبل المسيح بنحو مئة سنة، وكان وزير الإسكندر بن فِيْلبس المَقْدُوني الذي تؤرّخ له اليهود والنصارى التأريخ الرومي، وكان قد ذهب إلى أرض الفرس واستولى عليها .
وطائفة من الناس أنه كان وزير الإسكندر ذى القرنين المذكور في القرآن، وهذا جهل. فإن ذا القرنين كان مقدَّماً على أرسطو بمدة عظيمة، وكان مسلماً يعبد الله لم يكن مشركاً بخلاف المَقْدُوني. وذو القرنين بلغ أقصى المشرق والمغرب، وبنى السد
The Fourth Station: Strange beliefs of the philosophers
And they magnify the practical laws of the prophets. As for the theoretical ones, according to them knowledge in that is what the philosophers say. And as for the prophets, no knowledge is obtained from their direction regarding that.
Then among them are those who say that the prophet is greater than the philosopher, and they say: The prophet was inwardly upon the madhhab of these philosophers, but his special characteristic is imagination, even if it is false in reality for the benefit of the public. And among them are those who say: Rather the philosopher is greater than the prophet, and the prophet may not be inwardly knowledgeable about what is permissible for God and what is not, and the true nature of the matter regarding the afterlife, but he is skilled in laying down practical laws.
The author
And many of the heretical Sufis such as Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, al-Qunawi, al-Tilimsani and others agree with them in their principles, but they change the expressions and express with Islamic expressions what is their statement. And in the books restricted to those worthy of them and other books of their authors is a portion of this. And because of that, Ibn Arabi and the like of him among the heretical Sufis aligned with these people. And for this reason, the speech of the Muslim scholars regarding their authors increased. And among the people are those who deny that it is from the speech of Abu Hamid when they saw what is in them of great calamities. And others say: Rather he repented from that and his end was busy with al-Bukhari and Muslim, as has been mentioned in his biography. And these philosophers and their Sufis like Ibn Sab'in and his followers deem it permissible that a man be Jewish, Christian, or an idol-worshipping polytheist. So according to them, Islam is not obligatory, nor is Judaism, Christianity, and polytheism forbidden, but they may prefer the Sharia of Islam over others.
And when a seeker comes to a shaykh of their shaykhs and says: 'I want to follow your path', he says to him: 'Upon the religion of Muslims, or Jews, or Christians?' And if the seeker says to him: 'Are Jews and Christians disbelievers?' He says: 'No, but Muslims are better than them.' And this is from the type of the ignorant Tatars when they first embraced Islam. For Islam according to them is better than others, even if others are permissible; they do not ally on that basis nor take enmity on that basis.
And this is also the belief of most Christian scholars and many Jews. They see religion like the madhhabs of Muslims, and Jews and Christians like the madhhabs in the religion of Muslims, so it is permissible for a man according to them to transfer from this religious community to that, either because of its preferability according to him in religion, or for worldly benefit, just as a person transfers from the madhhab of some of the imams of the Muslims to another madhhab, such as transferring from the madhhab of Malik to al-Shafi'i, and from the madhhab of Abu Hanifa to the madhhab of Ahmad, and similar to that.
As for Aristotle and his companions, they were polytheists worshipping idols and planets. And such was the religion of the Greeks and Romans before the appearance of the religion of Christ among them. And Aristotle was about a hundred years before Christ, and he was the vizier of Alexander son of Philip the Macedonian, from whom the Jews and Christians date the Roman calendar, and he had gone to the land of Persia and conquered it.
And a group of people think that he was the vizier of Dhul-Qarnayn mentioned in the Quran, and this is ignorance. For Dhul-Qarnayn preceded Aristotle by a great time, and he was a Muslim worshipping God, not a polytheist, unlike the Macedonian. And Dhul-Qarnayn reached the farthest east and west, and built the dam.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya of the deviant views held by philosophers and their followers among heretical Sufis. He begins by contrasting how philosophers treat the practical and theoretical aspects of prophetic law: they respect the practical (sharia rulings) but consider theoretical knowledge (such as theology and metaphysics) as the domain of philosophy, not prophecy. Then he describes two factions among them: one that considers prophets superior but claims their teachings are merely imaginative representations (possibly false) for the public good, and another that considers philosophers superior and sees prophets as skilled only in practical legislation while ignorant of deeper truths about God and the afterlife. Next, Ibn Taymiyya links these ideas to heretical Sufis like Ibn Arabi and Ibn Sab'in, who adopt the same principles but cloak them in Islamic terminology. He notes the controversy over whether the works attributed to Abu Hamid al-Ghazali (the 'books restricted to those worthy') are genuine, with some denying them and others claiming he repented. Then he highlights a dangerous consequence: these philosophers and Sufis consider that a person can be a Jew, Christian, or idolater, and that Islam is not obligatory—merely preferred. He illustrates this with an anecdote of a seeker asking a shaykh about which religion to follow, and the shaykh's relativistic response. He compares this attitude to ignorant Tatars who accept Islam as better but permit other religions. He then observes that many Christian and Jewish scholars hold similar views, regarding the three religions as like different madhhabs within Islam, allowing transfer between them. Finally, he corrects a historical misconception: Aristotle was the vizier of Alexander the Macedonian (a polytheist), not of Dhul-Qarnayn (a righteous Muslim ruler), clarifying the distinction and emphasizing Dhul-Qarnayn's faith. Throughout, Ibn Taymiyya uses these examples to demonstrate how the philosophers' epistemological hierarchy (placing reason over revelation) leads to the undermining of Islam's exclusive truth claims and the necessity of following the Prophet.

Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that the philosophers' separation of practical from theoretical prophetic authority logically leads to religious relativism, which he refutes by affirming that prophetic truth encompasses both realms.

Exposing the False Analogy between Religions and Madhhabs
Author critiques those who treat Islam, Judaism, and Christianity as equally valid paths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the category error in equating different religions with Islamic legal schools and explain Ibn Taymiyya's critique of this relativism.

Core Idea
Treating religions as interchangeable madhhabs is a category error that denies Islam's exclusive truth.

In this passage from his refutation of the logicians, Ibn Taymiyya turns his critical eye to a relativistic trend among certain Sufi philosophers and scholars of other faiths. They treat Islam, Judaism, and Christianity as analogous to legal schools (madhhabs) within Islam, implying that switching religions is as permissible as switching from one fiqh school to another. Ibn Taymiyya exposes this as a profound confusion of categories with dangerous consequences for the exclusive truth of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of critique
Locate the view being criticized: that a seeker can choose any of the three religions, and that religions are like madhhabs. Note the sheikh's response to the seeker's question about Jews and Christians being disbelievers.
The sheikh denies they are disbelievers, merely saying Muslims are better.
2
Extract the false analogy
Compare the two things being equated: religions (Islam, Judaism, Christianity) vs. legal schools (madhhabs) within Islam. The basis of the analogy is that both are considered permissible paths.
Ibn Taymiyya points out that this view is held by some Christian and Jewish scholars as well.
3
Analyze the author's objection
Why does Ibn Taymiyya reject this analogy? He states that the seeker's question reveals the correct Islamic position (Jews and Christians are disbelievers), and the sheikh's denial is an error. He compares them to the ignorant Tatars who thought other religions were permissible.
The core objection: other religions are not permissible alternatives; they are false.
4
Understand the category error
The error is applying the internal Islamic concept of madhhab (legitimate diversity within a single truth) to the external relation between Islam and other religions. Madhhabs are valid interpretations within Islam, while other religions are invalid as paths to salvation.
This category mistake undermines the exclusive truth claim of Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا جاء المريدُ إلى شيخ من شيوخهم، وقال أريد أن أسلك على يديك، يقول له : على دين المسلمين، أو اليهود، أو النصارى؟» فإذا قال له المريد : «اليهود والنصارى أما هُم كُفَّار ؟ ) يقول : لا ، ولكن المسلمون خير منهم. وهذا من جنس جُهّال التَّتَر أَوَّلَ ما أسلموا . فإن الإسلام عندهم خير من غيره، وإن كان غيره جائزاً لا يُوالون عليه ويُعادون عليه . [٢٧٥] وهذا أيضاً أكثر اعتقاد علماء النصارى وكثير من اليهود. يرون دين بمنزلة مذاهب المسلمين واليهود والنصارى بمنزلة المذاهب في دين المسلمين فيجوز للرجل عندهم أن ينتقل من هذه الملة إلى تلك إما لرجحانها عنده في الدين، وإما لمصلحة دنياه، كما ينتقل الإنسان من مذهب بعض أئمة المسلمين إلى مذهب آخر، كما ينتقل من مذهب مالك إلى الشافعي، ومن مذهب أبي حنيفة إلى مذهب أحمد، ونحو ذلك .
And when the seeker comes to one of their sheikhs and says, 'I want to become your disciple,' he says to him: 'Upon the religion of the Muslims, or the Jews, or the Christians?' So if the seeker says to him, 'Are the Jews and Christians disbelievers?' He says, 'No, but the Muslims are better than them.' This is of the same kind as the ignorant Tatars when they first embraced Islam. For in their view, Islam is better than others, although others are permissible; they do not ally or oppose based on it. [275] This is also the belief of most Christian scholars and many Jews. They see religion as like the schools of thought within Islam; Judaism, Christianity, and Islam are like legal schools within the Muslim religion. Thus, in their view, it is permissible for a man to transfer from one religious community to another, either because he considers it more preponderant in religion or for worldly benefit, just as a person transfers from the school of some Muslim imams to another school, such as transferring from the school of Malik to al-Shafi'i, or from the school of Abu Hanifa to the school of Ahmad, and so on.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a critique of a dangerous intellectual error: treating different religions as if they were merely different legal schools (madhhabs) within Islam. Ibn Taymiyya begins by describing the practice of certain Sufi sheikhs who, when a seeker comes to them, offer a choice between Islam, Judaism, or Christianity as paths to God. When the seeker objects that Jews and Christians are disbelievers, the sheikh denies it, saying merely that Muslims are better. Ibn Taymiyya compares this to the ignorance of the early Tatars who had just converted. The core error is that they consider other religions permissible, even if inferior, so they do not take positions of loyalty or enmity based on religion. The author then extends this critique to Christian and Jewish scholars who view religions as equivalent to madhhabs, allowing conversion for perceived preference or worldly gain. He gives the analogy of switching from Maliki to Shafi'i school, which is valid within Islam, but to apply this to switching between Islam and other religions is a grave misapplication. This passage warns against the relativistic view that undermines the exclusive truth of Islam as the only acceptable religion before God.

مذهب
كفار

Key Takeaway

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Greek Polytheism
Author exposes polytheistic beliefs of Aristotle, Greeks, and later philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's historical and theological critique of Aristotelian philosophy and identify its key components.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya argues that Greek philosophy is rooted in polytheism, not reason.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya exposes the polytheistic origins of Greek philosophy, specifically targeting Aristotle and his followers. He does not merely dismiss philosophy as false; he provides historical evidence that the great Greek thinkers were idol worshippers. This critique is essential for understanding why Ibn Taymiyya rejects the epistemological authority of Greek logic and metaphysics. By analyzing his argument, you will learn how to deconstruct a philosophical tradition by examining its theological roots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of critique
Find the specific groups and individuals Ibn Taymiyya criticizes: Aristotle, his followers, the Greeks and Romans, and later philosophers (mutafalsifa).
He specifically names Aristotle as a minister of Alexander the Macedonian, distinguishing him from Dhul-Qarnayn.
2
Extract the historical evidence
List the historical claims Ibn Taymiyya uses: Aristotle lived 100 years before Christ, was a minister of Alexander, the Greeks and Romans were polytheistic before Christianity, etc.
He corrects a common confusion about Dhul-Qarnayn to show the Greek philosophers were not monotheists.
3
Analyze the theological accusation
Determine what acts of polytheism (shirk) he accuses them of: worshipping idols, celestial bodies (sun, moon, planets), building temples, and making talismans.
He compares this to the polytheism of Nimrod, the adversary of Prophet Abraham.
4
Connect to contemporary practices
Find how Ibn Taymiyya links ancient polytheism to later philosophers who outwardly practice Islam: they pray the five daily prayers but also worship celestial bodies or glorify Nimrod.
He gives a concrete example of someone who came to Damascus in 699 AH combining Islamic prayer with praise of Nimrod.
5
Evaluate the critique's validity
Assess whether Ibn Taymiyya's argument is compelling. Consider if it commits a genetic fallacy or if the historical evidence is sufficient to discredit the entire philosophical tradition.
His critique is based on historical and theological grounds, but one might argue that truth is independent of its source.

أرسطو ومشركوا اليونان: وأما أرسطو وأصحابه فكانوا مشركين يعبدون الأصنام والكواكب. وهكذا كان دين اليونان والروم قبل ظهور دين المسيح فيهم. وكان أرسطو قبل المسيح بنحو مئة سنة، وكان وزير الإسكندر بن فِيْلبس المَقْدُوني الذي تؤرّخ له اليهود والنصارى التأريخ الرومي، وكان قد ذهب إلى أرض الفرس واستولى عليها . وطائفة من الناس أنه كان وزير الإسكندر ذى القرنين المذكور في القرآن، وهذا جهل. فإن ذا القرنين كان مقدَّماً على أرسطو بمدة عظيمة، وكان مسلماً يعبد الله لم يكن مشركاً بخلاف المَقْدُوني. وذو القرنين بلغ أقصى المشرق والمغرب، وبنى سد يأجوج ومأجوج كما ذكر الله في كتابه والمقدوني لم يصل لا إلى هذا ولا إلى هذا، ولا وصل إلى السد . وآخر ملوكهم كان بَطْلَمِيوس صاحب المجِسْطي»، وبعده صاروا نصارى . وكانت اليونان والروم مشركين كما ذكر، يعبدون الشمس والقمر والكواكب، عبادة الكواكب ويبنون لها هَيَاكِلَ في الأرض ويصوّرون لها أصناماً يجعلون لها طلاسم، من جنس شرك النُّمْرُود بن كَنْعَان وقومه الذين بُعث إليهم إبراهيم الخليل - صلوات الله وسلامه عليه . وبقايا هذا الشرك في بلاد الشرق ـ في بلاد الخَطَا والتُرك . يصنعون الأصنام على صورة النمرود ، ويكون الصنم كبيراً جداً، ويعلقون السُّبَح في أعناقهم، ويسبحون باسم النمرود [٢٧٦] النمرود ، ويَشْتُمون إبراهيم الخليل . وكان من النفر القادمين إلى دمشق سنة تسع وتسعين وست مئة بعضُ هؤلاء. وهو نكت غريبة يجمع بين أن يصلي الصلوات الخمس وبين أن يسبّح باسم نمرود. وهذا أيضاً مذهب كثير من هؤلاء المتفلسفة وعلمائهم وعُبَّادهم يصلون الصلوات الخمس ويعبدون الشمس والقمر أو غيرهما من الكواكب. ومن هؤلاء طوائف موجودون في الشام، ومصر، والعراق، وغير ذلك وسبب ذلك أنه يحصل لهم أحياناً من جنس ما يَظهر للمشركين الذين كانوا يعبدون الكواكب والأصنام. فإنه كانت الشياطين تدخل في الصنم وتكلم عابديه، فتخبرهم بأمور مُكاشفة لهم، وتأمرهم بأمور يطلبون منهم قضاء حوائجهم .
Aristotle and the Polytheists of Greece: As for Aristotle and his followers, they were polytheists worshipping idols and celestial bodies. Such was the religion of the Greeks and Romans before the appearance of the Christian religion among them. Aristotle lived about one hundred years before Christ, and he was the minister of Alexander son of Philip the Macedonian, from whom the Jews and Christians date the Roman calendar, and he had gone to the land of Persia and conquered it. Some people claim that he was the minister of Dhul-Qarnayn mentioned in the Quran; this is ignorance. For Dhul-Qarnayn was much earlier than Aristotle, and he was a Muslim worshipping Allah, not a polytheist, unlike the Macedonian. Dhul-Qarnayn reached the farthest east and west, and built the dam of Gog and Magog as Allah mentioned in His Book, whereas the Macedonian did not reach either of these, nor did he reach the dam. The last of their kings was Ptolemy, author of the Almagest, and after him they became Christians. The Greeks and Romans were polytheists as mentioned, worshipping the sun, moon, and planets, building temples for them on earth, and making idols with talismans, of the same type as the polytheism of Nimrod son of Canaan and his people to whom Abraham the Friend of Allah was sent. Remnants of this polytheism exist in the eastern lands, in the lands of Khata and the Turks. They make idols in the image of Nimrod, the idol being very large, and they hang rosaries around their necks, and recite glorifications in the name of Nimrod, [276] and they curse Abraham. Some of these people were among the group that came to Damascus in the year 699 AH. It is a strange combination: he prays the five daily prayers and also glorifies the name of Nimrod. This is also the doctrine of many of these philosophers, their scholars and devotees: they pray the five daily prayers and worship the sun, moon, or other celestial bodies. Among them are groups found in Syria, Egypt, Iraq, and elsewhere. The reason for that is that sometimes they experience the same kind of things that appear to the polytheists who worshipped celestial bodies and idols: devils would enter the idol and speak to its worshippers, informing them of matters of unveiling and commanding them to do things to fulfill their needs.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological critique of Aristotelian philosophy and its polytheistic roots. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating plainly that Aristotle and his followers were polytheists who worshipped idols and celestial bodies. He contextualizes this by noting that the Greeks and Romans were polytheistic before Christianity. He then corrects a common confusion: some people mistakenly think Aristotle was the minister of Dhul-Qarnayn (the righteous king mentioned in the Quran). Ibn Taymiyya refutes this by pointing out that Dhul-Qarnayn lived much earlier, was a Muslim monotheist, and built the famous dam, while Aristotle's master Alexander the Macedonian did none of that. The author then mentions Ptolemy, the last Greek king and author of the Almagest, after whom the Greeks became Christian. He emphasizes that their polytheism involved worship of celestial bodies and idols, akin to the polytheism of Nimrod, the ancient tyrant opposed by Abraham. Ibn Taymiyya then shows that this polytheism persisted in the East, among the Turks and Khata, who make large idols of Nimrod and even curse Abraham. He gives a concrete example: some of these people came to Damascus in 699 AH, combining the five daily prayers with glorification of Nimrod. He concludes that this is the way of many philosophers and their followers: they outwardly perform Islamic prayers but internally worship celestial bodies. The reason, he explains, is that they experience demonic encounters similar to those of ancient idol worshippers—devils enter the idols and speak to them, providing supernatural experiences that they mistake for divine communion.

B) Because Dhul-Qarnayn was a Muslim monotheist who lived long before Aristotle, unlike the Macedonian polytheist.

D) Because Dhul-Qarnayn was a mythical figure not mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique reveals that for him, the theological roots of a tradition determine its validity; a polytheistic origin makes the entire philosophical enterprise suspect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
In a group, debate: Is Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Aristotle fair, or does it commit the genetic fallacy (judging an idea by its origin rather than its content)? Use the passage to support your position.

Ibn Taymiyya on the Two Origins of Shirk
Ibn Taymiyya details the polytheism of Greeks and Romans and identifies two origins of shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's two origins of shirk and explain how he uses historical evidence to support his claim.

Core Idea
All polytheism stems from grave-veneration or star-worship.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya traces the roots of polytheism (shirk) among ancient and contemporary peoples. He identifies two primary sources: the veneration of graves of righteous people, leading to image-making and eventually idolatry; and the worship of stars and planets, which he attributes to Greek and Roman philosophers. By linking these practices to the traditions of Nimrod and the people of Noah, Ibn Taymiyya provides a historical and theological critique that undermines the authority of Greek philosophical traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two origins
Read the passage and locate where Ibn Taymiyya explicitly states the two origins of shirk. They are: (1) veneration of graves of the righteous and making images for blessings, and (2) worship of stars and celestial bodies.
2
Analyze historical examples
Note the groups Ibn Taymiyya mentions: Greeks, Romans, Nimrod's people, Khata, Turks, and contemporary groups in Syria, Egypt, Iraq. How does each exemplify one of the two origins?
3
Understand the theological link
Ibn Taymiyya connects star-worship to Nimrod and grave-worship to the people of Noah. Reflect on why these links are significant in Islamic salvation history.
4
Recognize the role of devils
Ibn Taymiyya mentions that devils would enter idols and speak to worshippers. How does this explain the persistence and appeal of polytheistic practices?
5
Evaluate the inductive argument
Assess whether the examples given are sufficient to establish the two origins as universal. Is this an inductive generalization? Is it complete or incomplete?

المقام الرابع - أرسطو ومشركوا اليونان. يأجوج ومأجوج كما ذكر الله في كتابه والمقدوني لم يصل لا إلى هذا ولا إلى هذا، ولا وصل إلى السد. وآخر ملوكهم كان بَطْلَمِيوس (۱) صاحب المجِسْطي»، وبعده صاروا نصارى . وكانت اليونان والروم مشركين كما ذكر، يعبدون الشمس والقمر والكواكب، عبادة الكواكب ويبنون لها هَيَاكِلَ في الأرض ويصوّرون لها أصناماً يجعلون لها طلاسم، من جنس شرك النُّمْرُود بن كَنْعَان (۲) وقومه الذين بُعث إليهم إبراهيم الخليل - صلوات الله وسلامه عليه . وبقايا هذا الشرك في بلاد الشرق ـ في بلاد الخَطَا والتُرك . يصنعون الأصنام على الأصنام التي على صورة صورة النمرود ، ويكون الصنم كبيراً جداً، ويعلقون السُّبَح في أعناقهم، ويسبحون باسم النمرود النمرود ، ويَشْتُمون إبراهيم الخليل . وكان من النفر القادمين إلى دمشق سنة تسع وتسعين وست مئة بعضُ هؤلاء. وهو نكت غريبة يجمع بين أن يصلي الصلوات الخمس وبين أن يسبّح باسم نمرود. وهذا أيضاً مذهب كثير من هؤلاء المتفلسفة وعلمائهم وعُبَّادهم يصلون الصلوات الخمس ويعبدون الشمس والقمر أو غيرهما من الكواكب. ومن هؤلاء طوائف موجودون في الشام، ومصر، والعراق، وغير ذلك وسبب ذلك أنه يحصل لهم أحياناً من جنس ما يَظهر للمشركين الذين كانوا يعبدون الكواكب والأصنام. فإنه كانت الشياطين تدخل في الصنم وتكلّم عابديه، فتخبرهم بأمور مُكاشفة لهم، وتأمرهم بأمور يطلبون منهم قضاء حوائجهم . ثم ذكر قصة العزى واللات ومناة، وأصل الشرك من تعظيم القبور وعبادة الكواكب. والشرك [٢٧٧] في بني آدم أكثره عن أصلين : أولهما: تعظيم قبور الصالحين وتصوير تماثيلهم للتبرك بها. وهذا أول الأسباب التي بها ابتدع الآدميون الشرك. وهو شرك قوم نوح. قال ابن عباس : كان بين آدم ونوح عشرة قرون كلهم على الإسلام. وقد ثبت في الصحيح عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نوحاً
The fourth station - Aristotle and the polytheists of Greece. Gog and Magog as God mentioned in His Book, and the Macedonian did not reach this nor that, nor did he reach the dam. And the last of their kings was Ptolemy, the author of the Almagest, and after him they became Christians. The Greeks and Romans were polytheists as mentioned, worshipping the sun, moon, and stars, the worship of stars, and they built for them temples in the earth and fashioned for them idols, making for them talismans, of the same kind as the polytheism of Nimrod son of Canaan and his people to whom Abraham the Friend (peace be upon him) was sent. Remnants of this polytheism exist in the lands of the East – in the lands of Khata and the Turks. They make idols upon the idols that were in the image of the image of Nimrod, and the idol is very large, and they hang rosaries around their necks, and they glorify in the name of Nimrod, and they curse Abraham the Friend. And there were among the group arriving in Damascus in the year 699 AH some of these. It is a strange matter that combines performing the five daily prayers and glorifying in the name of Nimrod. And this is also the doctrine of many of these pseudo-philosophers and their scholars and devotees: they perform the five prayers and worship the sun and moon or other heavenly bodies. Among them are groups present in Syria, Egypt, Iraq, and elsewhere. The reason for that is that sometimes they experience the kind of thing that appears to the polytheists who used to worship the stars and idols. For the devils used to enter the idol and speak to its worshippers, informing them of matters of unveiling for them, and commanding them with matters, and they would ask them to fulfill their needs. Then he mentioned the story of al-‘Uzza, al-Lat, and Manat, and the origin of polytheism is from the veneration of graves and the worship of stars. And polytheism in mankind mostly arises from two origins: First: the veneration of the graves of the righteous and making images of them for seeking blessings. This is the first cause by which mankind innovated polytheism. It is the polytheism of the people of Noah. Ibn ‘Abbas said: Between Adam and Noah there were ten generations, all of them upon Islam. And it is established in the Sahih from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that Noah...
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological critique by Ibn Taymiyya, aimed at exposing the polytheistic roots of Greek philosophy. He begins by stating that the Greeks and Romans were polytheists who worshipped the sun, moon, and stars, building temples and idols, similar to the polytheism of Nimrod. He then notes that remnants of this star-worship persist among Eastern peoples like the Khata and Turks, who make large idols and glorify Nimrod's name. Ibn Taymiyya highlights a strange phenomenon: some people in his time combine Islamic prayer with polytheistic practices like glorifying Nimrod. He attributes this to the influence of devils who would enter idols and speak to their worshippers, providing them with supernatural information. Finally, he states that polytheism among mankind originates from two main sources: first, the veneration of graves of righteous people and making images of them for blessings, which was the polytheism of Noah's people; and second, the worship of stars and heavenly bodies. The passage serves to discredit Greek philosophical traditions by tying them to ancient polytheism.

The Two Origins of Shirk: Grave Veneration and Star Worship
Ibn Taymiyya enumerates and details the two primary origins of shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the two primary origins of shirk according to Ibn Taymiyya, and trace their historical roots as presented in this passage.

Core Idea
Shirk emerges from two roots: reverence of graves and worship of stars.

Ibn Taymiyya, in his critique of deviant beliefs, traces the majority of shirk among humans to two origins. This passage explains how the veneration of righteous individuals after death led to idolatry in Noah's time, and how astrological practices of the Chaldeans involved worship of celestial bodies. Understanding these roots is essential for diagnosing contemporary forms of shirk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two origins
Locate the opening statement: 'والشرك في بني آدم أكثره عن أصلين'. Determine what the two origins are according to the passage.
2
Examine the first origin
Explain how grave veneration of righteous people led to shirk among Noah's people. Note the Quranic verse and Ibn Abbas' report.
3
Examine the second origin
Describe the practice of star worship: talismans, timing, and the role of devils (ruhaniyya).
4
Note historical references
Why does Ibn Taymiyya mention Noah and Abraham? How does this connect to the genealogy of shirk?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشرك في بني آدم أكثره عن أصلين: أولهما: تعظيم قبور الصالحين وتصوير تماثيلهم للتبرك بها. وهذا أول الأسباب التي بها ابتدع الآدميون الشرك. وهو شرك قوم نوح. قال ابن عباس: كان بين آدم ونوح عشرة قرون كلهم على الإسلام. وقد ثبت في الصحيح عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نوحاً أول رسول بُعث إلى أهل الأرض. ولهذا لم يذكر الله في القرآن قبله رسولاً. فإن الشرك إنما ظهر في زمانه. وقد ذكر البخاري في صحيحه عن ابن عباس وذكره أهل التفسير والسير عن أول عبادة غير واحد من السلف، في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَقَالُوا لَا تَذَرُنَّ آلِهَتَكُمْ وَلَا تَذَرُنَّ وَذًّا وَلَا سُوَاعًا وَلَا يَغُونَ وَيَعُوقَ وَنَسْرًا ﴾ [سورة نوح: 23]. أن هؤلاء كانوا قوماً صالحين في قوم نوح، فلما ماتوا عكفوا على قبورهم، ثم صوّروا تماثيلهم. وأن هذه الأصنام صارت إلى العرب. وذكر ابن عباس قبائل العرب التي كانت فيهم مثل هذه الأصنام. والسبب الثاني: عبادة الكواكب. فكانوا يصنعون للأصنام طلاسم للكواكب، ويتحرون الوقت المناسب لصنعة ذلك الطَّلَّسْم، ويصنعونه من مادة تناسب ما يرونه من طبيعة ذلك الكوكب، ويتكلمون عليها بالشرك والكفر. فتأتي الشياطين، فتكلمهم، وتقضي بعض حوائجهم ويسمونها «روحانية الكواكب»، وهي الشيطان أو الشيطانة التي تُضلّهم. والكتاب الذي صنفه بعضُ الناس وسماه السرّ المكتوم في السحر ومخاطبة النجوم، فإن هذا كان شرك الكلدانيين والكشدانيين. وهم الذين بعث إليهم إبراهيم الخليل عليه السلام.
And shirk among the children of Adam is mostly from two origins: The first of them: veneration of the graves of the righteous and making images of them for blessing. And this is the first of the causes by which the humans innovated shirk. And it is the shirk of the people of Noah. Ibn Abbas said: Between Adam and Noah were ten generations, all upon Islam. And it is established in the Sahih from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that Noah was the first messenger sent to the people of the earth. And for this, God did not mention in the Quran a messenger before him. For shirk only appeared in his time. And al-Bukhari mentioned in his Sahih from Ibn Abbas, and the people of tafsir and siyar mentioned from more than one of the salaf, regarding the saying of the Exalted: 'And they said: Do not forsake your gods, and do not forsake Wadd, nor Suwa', nor Yaghuth, nor Ya'uq, nor Nasr' [Surah Nuh: 23]. That these were righteous people among the people of Noah. When they died, they secluded themselves at their graves, then they made images of them. And these idols ended up with the Arabs. And Ibn Abbas mentioned the Arab tribes among whom were such idols. And the second cause: worship of the planets. They used to make talismans for the idols for the planets, and they would seek the opportune time for making that talisman, and they would make it from a material suitable for what they saw of the nature of that planet, and they would speak upon them with shirk and disbelief. Then the devils would come, speak to them, and fulfill some of their needs, and they call them 'the spirituality of the planets', and it is the devil or the she-devil that misguides them. And the book that some people authored and named 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' concerning sorcery and addressing the stars, for this was the shirk of the Chaldeans and the Kasdanians. And they are those to whom Abraham the Friend, peace be upon him, was sent.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya of the origins of shirk (polytheism) among humans. He states that the majority of shirk arises from two roots. The first is excessive veneration of graves of righteous people and making images of them for blessings. He traces this back to the people of Noah, citing the Quranic verse listing their idols. Ibn Abbas is quoted to establish that between Adam and Noah there were ten generations all upon monotheism, and shirk only appeared in Noah's time. He then explains that the righteous people after their deaths were venerated, leading to image-making and eventually idol worship that passed to the Arabs. The second origin is worship of celestial bodies (planets). People made talismans for idols corresponding to planets, timed their making astrologically, and attributed spiritual powers to the devils that spoke to them. He mentions a book called 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' on sorcery and astral communication, linking this practice to the Chaldeans, to whom Prophet Abraham was sent. This classification helps understand the historical and theological roots of false beliefs, a key theme in Ibn Taymiyya's critique of deviant practices.

شرك
تعظيم القبور
عبادة الكواكب
روحانية الكواكب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya identifies grave veneration and star worship as the two historical wellsprings of shirk, tracing each to specific pre-Islamic peoples.

Ibn Taymiyya on the Origins of Shirk: Grave Worship and Star Worship
Ibn Taymiyya on the two historical causes of shirk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between grave worship and star worship as two distinct origins of shirk according to Ibn Taymiyya, and evaluate his claim that astrology is a branch of sorcery.

Core Idea
Shirk originated from excessive veneration of the dead and from worship of the planets, both rooted in devilish deception.

In this passage from his critique of the logicians, Ibn Taymiyya takes a historical turn to explain how polytheism first appeared among mankind. He identifies two primary causes: the veneration of graves of righteous people, as in the story of Noah's people, and the worship of planets through talismans and astrology. Understanding this historical analysis is key to appreciating his broader argument that many intellectual traditions, including certain forms of logic and natural philosophy, are tainted by pagan origins.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two causal claims
Find the sentences where Ibn Taymiyya states the two origins. He introduces the first with 'أصل الشرك من تعظيم القبور' and transitions to the second with 'والسبب الثاني: عبادة الكواكب'. Notice the clear demarcation.
The passage begins with 'المقام الرابع' indicating this is the fourth topic.
2
Extract the mechanism of grave worship
From the Quranic verse (Nuh 71:23) and the report of Ibn Abbas, trace the chain: righteous people died, people venerated their graves, then made images, which eventually became idols worshipped by Arabs. Identify how veneration escalated to shirk.
Ibn Taymiyya uses tafsir and sira to ground this historical account.
3
Extract the mechanism of star worship
Identify the practices: making talismans for planets, seeking astrologically favorable times, using materials corresponding to planetary natures, and claiming 'spirituality of the planets'. Note how Ibn Taymiyya reinterprets that spirituality as devils speaking to practitioners.
He calls the practitioners 'Chaldeans' and links them to Abraham's mission.
4
Assess his identification of astrology with sorcery
Find the hadith he cites ('Whoever acquires a branch of astrology has acquired a branch of sorcery') and his list of books and authors (Tankalusha, Tintim, Abu Ma'shar, Thabit ibn Qurra). How does he argue that these are forms of shirk and sorcery?
He claims to have seen and refuted the contents of 'al-Sirr al-Maktum'.
5
Synthesize the two causes into his broader critique
Consider how both causes involve human practices that are claimed to be spiritual but are actually devilish deceptions. This supports Ibn Taymiyya's overall project of purifying Islamic practice from pagan influences.
This passage is part of a larger work critiquing Greek logic as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - أصل الشرك من تعظيم القبور وعبادة الكواكب
أول رسول بُعث إلى أهل الأرض. ولهذا لم يذكر الله في القرآن قبله رسولاً. فإن الشرك إنما ظهر في زمانه.
وقد ذكر البخاري في صحيحه عن ابن عباس وذكره أهل التفسير والسير عن أول عبادة غير واحد من السلف، في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَقَالُوا لَا تَذَرُنَّ آلِهَتَكُمْ وَلَا تَذَرُنَّ وَدًّا وَلَا سُوَاعًا وَلَا يَغُوثَ وَيَعُوقَ وَنَسْرًا ﴾ [سورة نوح: 23]. أن هؤلاء كانوا قوماً صالحين في قوم نوح، فلما ماتوا عكفوا على قبورهم، ثم صوّروا تماثيلهم. وأن هذه الأصنام صارت إلى العرب. وذكر ابن عباس قبائل العرب التي كانت فيهم مثل هذه الأصنام.
والسبب الثاني: عبادة الكواكب. فكانوا يصنعون للأصنام طلاسم للكواكب، ويتحرون الوقت المناسب لصنعة ذلك الطَّلَّسْم، ويصنعونه من مادة تناسب ما يرونه من طبيعة ذلك الكوكب، ويتكلمون عليها بالشرك والكفر. فتأتي الشياطين، فتكلمهم، وتقضي بعض حوائجهم ويسمونها «روحانية الكواكب»، وهي الشيطان أو الشيطانة التي تُضلّهم.
والكتاب الذي صنفه بعضُ الناس وسماه السرّ المكتوم في السحر ومخاطبة كتاب السر المكتوم، فإن هذا كان شرك الكلدانيين والكشدانيين. وهم الذين بعث إليهم الخليل - صلوات الله عليه. وهذا أعظم أنواع السحر ولهذا قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الحديث الذي رواه أبو داود وغيره: «مَنْ اقتبس شُعبةً مِن النجوم فقد اقتبس شعبةً من السِّحر، زادَ ما زاد». وقد رأيتُه وبينتُ ما فيه من الفساد، فإن فيه ضلالاً كثيراً. ولهذا صنف تنكُلُوشا البابلي كتابه في درجات الفلك. وكذلك شرك الهند وسحرهم من هذا، مثل كتاب طِمْطِم الهندي. وكذلك أبو مَعْشَر البَلْخِي في النجوم له كتاب سماه مصحف القمر. وكذلك ثابت بن قُرَّة الحراني صاحب الزيج.
The fourth station - The origin of shirk is from the veneration of graves and the worship of planets. The first messenger sent to the people of the earth. For this reason, Allah did not mention before him a messenger in the Quran. Indeed, shirk only appeared in his time. And al-Bukhari mentioned in his Sahih on the authority of Ibn Abbas, and the people of tafsir and sirah mentioned it regarding the first worship, more than one of the Salaf, regarding His statement: 'And they said: Do not abandon your gods, nor abandon Wadd, nor Suwa', nor Yaghuth, nor Ya'uq, nor Nasr' [Surah Nuh: 23]. That these were righteous people among the people of Noah, and when they died, they secluded at their graves, then they made images of them. And that these idols passed to the Arabs. And Ibn Abbas mentioned the Arab tribes among whom these idols were. And the second cause: worship of the planets. They used to make talismans for the idols for the planets, and they would seek the appropriate time for making that talisman, and make it from material that suits what they see of the nature of that planet, and they spoke about them with shirk and kufr. Then the devils come, and speak to them, and fulfill some of their needs, and they call them 'the spirituality of the planets', and they are the male devil or female devil that leads them astray. And the book that some people wrote and named it 'The Hidden Secret in Sorcery and the Communication with the Book of the Hidden Secret' - this was the shirk of the Chaldeans and the Kasdanians. And they are the ones to whom al-Khalil (peace be upon him) was sent. And this is the greatest type of sorcery. For this reason, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in the hadith narrated by Abu Dawud and others: 'Whoever acquires a branch of astrology has acquired a branch of sorcery, increasing as it increases.' And I have seen it and explained what corruption it contains, for it contains much misguidance. For this reason, Tankalusha the Babylonian wrote his book on the degrees of the sphere. Likewise, the shirk of India and their sorcery is from this, such as the book of Tintim the Indian. Also, Abu Ma'shar al-Balkhi has a book on astrology named 'The Mushaf of the Moon'. Also, Thabit ibn Qurra al-Harrani, the author of the Zij.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya on the historical origins of polytheism (shirk). He divides the causes into two: first, the veneration of graves, and second, the worship of planets (astrology). He begins by noting that the first messenger was sent to the people of the earth, implying that shirk emerged later. He cites the Quranic verse from Surah Nuh (71:23) and the commentary that the names mentioned were those of righteous people whose graves were venerated, leading to idol worship. He then transitions to the second cause: planet worship, where people made talismans for the planets, sought astrologically favorable times, and attributed their practices to the 'spirituality of the planets', which Ibn Taymiyya identifies as devils. He mentions specific books and figures, such as 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' attributed to al-Razi, which he considers Chaldean shirk and sorcery. He quotes the hadith that astrology is a branch of sorcery. Then he lists several works and authors, such as Tankalusha's 'Daraj al-Falak', the Indian book 'Tintim', Abu Ma'shar's 'Mushaf al-Qamar', and Thabit ibn Qurra's 'Zij', all of which he regards as examples of shirk and sorcery. Throughout, Ibn Taymiyya is arguing that these practices are not merely errors but are rooted in pagan shirk, thereby critiquing the intellectual traditions that rely on astrology and associated sciences.

Key Terms
شرك
عبادة القبور
عبادة الكواكب
طلاسم
روحانية الكواكب
سحر

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to Ibn Taymiyya, what are the two main historical causes of shirk?
A) Grave worship and star worship
B) Idol worship and ancestor worship
C) Nature worship and sun worship
D) Worship of kings and worship of angels

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya traces shirk to two historical roots: grave veneration (originating with Noah's people) and planet worship (originating with the Chaldeans), both of which he considers devilish deceptions.

Using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria, analyze a contemporary practice (e.g., seeking astrological readings) – identify which elements correspond to the star worship mechanism he describes.
?

Sabians: Monotheists and Polytheists in Ibn Taymiyya
Definition and classification of Sabians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of Sabians as defined by Ibn Taymiyya and identify which are praised in the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Not all Sabians were polytheists; the Qur'an praises monotheist Sabians.

Ibn Taymiyya uses historical and Qur'anic analysis to refine the understanding of the term 'Sabian'. This distinction is crucial for evaluating the origins of philosophical doctrines, as he later links the polytheist Sabians to Aristotle's claim of an eternal world. Here we focus on the classification itself.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Qur'anic verses on Sabians
Read Surah al-Baqarah:62 and Surah al-Hajj:17. Notice that the first promises reward to Sabians who believe in Allah and the Last Day, while the second lists Sabians among those Allah will judge without such praise.
The verses are quoted in this passage.
2
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's two-fold division
He says: 'The Sabians are of two types: Sabians who are monotheist Hanifs and Sabians who are polytheists.' The first are praised in al-Baqarah, the second are not.
Key Arabic: الصابئة نوعان: صابئة حنفاء موحدون وصابئة مشركون.
3
Connect the praised Sabians to earlier monotheists
Ibn Taymiyya states that the praised Sabians followed the religion of Abraham (Hanifs) before the Torah and Gospel, or the original scriptures before alteration.
This makes them part of the same category as righteous Jews and Christians.
4
Contrast with polytheists and Magians
He notes that in Surah al-Hajj, Allah lists six groups including Magians and polytheists, and does not say any of them are believers—only the four groups in al-Baqarah include believers.
This supports his claim that only some Sabians are praiseworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - حران دار الصابئة
فإن حرّان (۱) كانت دار هؤلاء الصابئة وفيها ولد إبراهيم، أو انتقل إليها من مولد إبراهيم العراق، على اختلاف القولين.
وكان بها هيكل العلة الأولى هيكل العقل الأول)، هيكل «النفس الكلية»، الهياكل التي هيكل زُحل هيكل المُشْتَري هيكل المريخ (۲) ، هيكل الشمس. وكذلك الزهرة، بحران وعُطَارِد، والقمر . وكان هذا دينهم قبل ظهور النصرانية فيهم. ثم ظهرت النصرانية فيهم مع بقاء أولئك الصابئة المشركين حتى جاء الإسلام. ولم يزل بها الصابئة والفلاسفة في دولة الإسلام إلى آخر وقت . ومنهم الصابئة الذين كانوا ببغداد وغيرها أطباء وكتاباً، وبعضهم لم يسلم .
ولما قدم الفارابي (۳) حَرَّان في أثناء المئة الرابعة دخل عليهم، وتعلم منهم، وأخذ ما أخذ المتفلسفة. وكان ثابت بن قُرَّة قد شرح كلام أرسطو في الإلهيات، وقد رأيته وبينتُ بعض ما فيه من الفساد. فإن فيه ضلالاً كثيراً.
وكذلك كان دين أهل دمشق وغيرها قبل ظهور دين النصرانية. وكانوا يصلون إلى دين أهل النحلة، توفي سنة ٢٨٨ هـ .
دمشق
القطب الشمالي. ولهذا توجد في دمشق مساجد قديمة فيها قبلة إلى القطب الشمالي . وتحت جامع دمشق معبد كبير له قبلةٌ إلى القطب الشمالي كان لهؤلاء .
الصابئة نوعان فإن الصابئة نوعان : صابئة حُنَفاء موحدون وصابئة مشركون. فالأولون هم الذين أثنى الله عليهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا وَالنَّصَرَىٰ وَالصَّابِئِينَ مَنْ آمَنَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَعَمِلَ صَالِحًا فَلَهُمْ أَجْرُهُمْ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ وَلَا خَوْفٌ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا هُمْ يَحْزَنُونَ ﴾ [سورة البقرة : ٦٢] . فأثنى على من آمن بالله واليوم الآخر وعمل صالحاً من هذه الملل الأربع المؤمنين واليهود والنصارى، والصابئين.
فهؤلاء كانوا يدينون بالتوراة قبل النسخ والتبديل. وكذلك الذين دانوا بالإنجيل قبل النسخ والتبديل والصابئون الذين كانوا قبل هؤلاء كالمتبعين لملة إبراهيم الحُنفاء - صلى الله عليه وصلى الله على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما صلى على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم، إنه حميد مجيد - قبل نزول التوراة والإنجيل .
وهذا بخلاف المجوس والمشركين، فإنه ليس فيهم مؤمن . فلهذا قال الله تعالى : إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا وَالصَّابِئِينَ وَالنَّصَرَى وَالْمَجُوسَ وَالَّذِينَ أَشْرَكُوا إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَفْصِلُ بيْنَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ شَهِيدٌ ﴾ [سورة الحج : ١٧]. فذكر الملل الستّ هؤلاء، وأخبر أنه يفصل بينهم يوم القيامة. لم يذكر في الستُ من كان مؤمناً، وإنما ذكر ذلك في الأربعة فقط
.
/
ثم إن الصابئين ابتدعوا الشرك فصاروا مشركين والفلاسفة المشركون من هؤلاء المشركين وأما قدماء الفلاسفة الذين كانوا يعبدون الله وحده لا يشركون به شيئاً، ويؤمنون بأن الله مُحدث لهذا العالم ويُقرون بمعاد الأبدان، فأولئك من الصابئة الحنفاء الذين أثنى الله عليهم .
أول من ظهر ثم المشركون من الصابئة كانوا يقرّون بحدوث هذا العالم، كما كان المشركون بقدم العالم من العرب تُقرّ بحدوثه، وكذلك المشركون من الهند . وقد ذكر أهل المقالات أن أول من ظهر عنه القول بقدمه من هؤلاء الفلاسفة المشركين هو أرسطو .
The Fourth Station - Harran, the abode of the Sabians. For Harran was the abode of these Sabians, and in it Abraham was born, or he moved to it from his birthplace in Iraq, according to the two differing opinions. In it were the Temple of the First Cause, the Temple of the First Intellect, the Temple of the Universal Soul, the temples: the Temple of Saturn, the Temple of Jupiter, the Temple of Mars, the Temple of the Sun, likewise Venus, Mercury, and the Moon in Harran. This was their religion before the appearance of Christianity among them. Then Christianity appeared among them while those polytheist Sabians remained until Islam came. The Sabians and philosophers persisted there in the Islamic state until the last time. Among them were the Sabians who were in Baghdad and elsewhere as physicians and scribes, and some of them did not convert to Islam. When al-Farabi came to Harran during the fourth century, he entered upon them, learned from them, and took what the philosophers took. Thabit ibn Qurra had commented on Aristotle's words on metaphysics, and I have seen it and explained some of the corruption in it, for it contains much error. Likewise was the religion of the people of Damascus and others before the appearance of Christianity. They prayed facing the North Pole. For this reason, in Damascus there are ancient mosques with prayer niches facing the North Pole. Under the Umayyad Mosque in Damascus is a large temple with a prayer niche facing the North Pole that belonged to these people. The Sabians are of two types: monotheist Hanif Sabians and polytheist Sabians. The former are those whom Allah praised in His saying: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews and Christians and Sabians, whoever believed in Allah and the Last Day and did righteousness—will have their reward with their Lord, and no fear will there be concerning them, nor will they grieve.' So He praised those who believe in Allah and the Last Day and do righteousness from among these four religions: the believers, the Jews, the Christians, and the Sabians. These were followers of the Torah before the abrogation and alteration, and likewise those who followed the Gospel before abrogation and alteration, and the Sabians who were before these, like the followers of the religion of Abraham the Hanif—peace be upon him and upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad as He sent blessings upon Abraham and the family of Abraham, indeed He is Praiseworthy, Glorious—before the revelation of the Torah and the Gospel. This is contrary to the Magians and polytheists, for among them there is no believer. For this reason Allah said: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews and Sabians and Christians and Magians and those who associated with Allah—indeed Allah will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection. Indeed Allah is, over all things, Witness.' So He mentioned these six religions and informed that He will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection. He did not mention in the six any who was a believer; rather He mentioned that only in the four. Then the Sabians innovated polytheism and became polytheists, and the polytheist philosophers are among these polytheists. As for the ancient philosophers who used to worship Allah alone, not associating anything with Him, and believed that Allah is the Creator of this world, and affirmed the resurrection of bodies—those are among the Hanif Sabians whom Allah praised. Then the polytheists among the Sabians used to affirm the temporal origination of this world, just as the polytheists among the Arabs used to affirm its temporal origination, and likewise the polytheists among the Indians. The authors of doctrinal works have mentioned that the first from whom the statement of its eternity appeared among these polytheist philosophers was Aristotle.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a historical and doctrinal exposition by Ibn Taymiyya in which he traces the origins of philosophical doctrines, particularly the claim of the eternity of the world, back to the polytheist branch of the Sabians. The passage functions as a critique of the philosophers by showing that their core belief (qidam al-‘ālam) has a dubious origin. The author begins by describing Harran as the center of the Sabians, mentioning the temples dedicated to celestial bodies and abstract entities like the First Cause, First Intellect, and Universal Soul. This sets the stage: the Sabians were originally star-worshippers. He notes that Christianity and later Islam spread among them, but some Sabians remained polytheists. Importantly, al-Farabi studied with them, and Thabit ibn Qurra, a Sabian, commented on Aristotle’s metaphysics. Ibn Taymiyya claims to have seen this commentary and found it corrupt. He then shifts to the Sabians themselves, declaring that there are two types: monotheist Hanif Sabians and polytheist Sabians. The monotheists are those praised in the Qur’an (Surah al-Baqarah: 62) for believing in Allah and the Last Day and doing righteous deeds. They followed the original Torah and Gospel before abrogation, or the religion of Abraham before the scriptures. In contrast, the Magians and polytheists have no believers among them, as indicated in Surah al-Hajj: 17, where Allah lists six groups but does not praise any of them. Then Ibn Taymiyya explains that the Sabians later innovated polytheism, and the polytheist philosophers (including Aristotle) belong to this branch. However, the ancient philosophers who were monotheists and believed in creation and bodily resurrection are among the praised Hanif Sabians. Finally, he notes that the polytheist Sabians initially affirmed the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of the world, even the Arabs and Indians did so. The first to claim the eternity of the world (qidam) among the polytheist philosophers was Aristotle. Thus, Ibn Taymiyya argues that the doctrine of the world’s eternity is a later innovation, not an ancient truth, and comes from the polytheist Sabians, not the original monotheists.

Key Terms
الصابئة
الحنفاء
المشركون

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, which type of Sabians are praised in Surah al-Baqarah:62?
A) The polytheist Sabians who worshipped celestial bodies
B) The monotheist Hanif Sabians who believed in Allah and the Last Day
C) All Sabians without distinction
D) The Sabians who followed al-Farabi and Aristotle

Key Takeaway
The term 'Sabian' is not monolithic; the Qur'an distinguishes between monotheist Hanifs and polytheists, and only the former are praised.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read Surah al-Baqarah:62 and Surah al-Hajj:17. According to Ibn Taymiyya, why does the first verse praise some Sabians while the second does not? Write a two-sentence explanation in your own words.
?
Identify the genus (جنس) and differentia (فصل) in Ibn Taymiyya's definition of the Sabians. The genus is the broader category (Sabians), and the differentia is the distinguishing characteristic (monotheist vs. polytheist). Write them down.

The Origin of the Doctrine of the World's Eternity
Genealogical critique of the eternity doctrine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's historical argument that the doctrine of the world's eternity (qidam al-‘ālam) originated from the polytheist Sabians and was first articulated by Aristotle.

Core Idea
Aristotle's eternal world was a later innovation from polytheist star-worshippers, not an ancient truth.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya advances a genealogical critique: he traces the philosophical claim that the world is eternal back to the polytheist branch of the Sabians in Harran. By linking Aristotle to these polytheists, he undermines the authority of the philosophers. We will follow his chain of transmission and evaluate his argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doctrine under attack
The doctrine is 'qidam al-‘ālam' – that the world is eternal, without beginning. This is a central claim of Aristotle and the Peripatetic philosophers.
Ibn Taymiyya contrasts it with the Islamic belief in creation (ḥudūth).
2
Trace the geographic and religious origin
Ibn Taymiyya identifies Harran as the center of the Sabians, specifically the polytheist ones who worshipped stars and built temples to planets and abstract entities like the First Intellect. This is the environment from which the doctrine emerged.
He mentions temples to Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, etc., and to the First Cause, First Intellect, and Universal Soul.
3
Note the role of key transmitters
Al-Farabi came to Harran and studied with these Sabians; Thabit ibn Qurra, a Sabian, commented on Aristotle's metaphysics. Ibn Taymiyya claims to have seen Thabit's commentary and found it corrupt.
This shows how Greek philosophy was transmitted through polytheist channels.
4
Pinpoint the first proponent of the doctrine
Ibn Taymiyya states explicitly: 'The first from whom the statement of its eternity appeared among these polytheist philosophers was Aristotle.' Before him, even polytheist Sabians, Arabs, and Indians affirmed temporal origination (ḥudūth).
Thus Aristotle innovated the claim of eternity, deviating from earlier Sabian belief.

المقام الرابع - حران دار الصابئة

وكان بها هيكل العلة الأولى هيكل العقل الأول)، هيكل «النفس الكلية»، الهياكل التي هيكل زُحل هيكل المُشْتَري هيكل المريخ (۲) ، هيكل الشمس. وكذلك الزهرة، بحران وعُطَارِد، والقمر . وكان هذا دينهم قبل ظهور النصرانية فيهم. ثم ظهرت النصرانية فيهم مع بقاء أولئك الصابئة المشركين حتى جاء الإسلام. ولم يزل بها الصابئة والفلاسفة في دولة الإسلام إلى آخر وقت . ومنهم الصابئة الذين كانوا ببغداد وغيرها أطباء وكتاباً، وبعضهم لم يسلم .
ولما قدم الفارابي (۳) حَرَّان في أثناء المئة الرابعة دخل عليهم، وتعلم منهم، وأخذ ما أخذ المتفلسفة. وكان ثابت بن قُرَّة قد شرح كلام أرسطو في الإلهيات، وقد رأيته وبينتُ بعض ما فيه من الفساد. فإن فيه ضلالاً كثيراً.
