دمشق
القطب الشمالي. ولهذا توجد في دمشق مساجد قديمة فيها قبلة إلى القطب الشمالي . وتحت جامع دمشق معبد كبير له قبلةٌ إلى القطب الشمالي كان لهؤلاء .
الصابئة نوعان فإن الصابئة نوعان : صابئة حُنَفاء موحدون وصابئة مشركون. فالأولون هم الذين أثنى الله عليهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا وَالنَّصَرَىٰ وَالصَّابِئِينَ مَنْ آمَنَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَعَمِلَ صَالِحًا فَلَهُمْ أَجْرُهُمْ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ وَلَا خَوْفٌ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا هُمْ يَحْزَنُونَ ﴾ [سورة البقرة : ٦٢] . فأثنى على من آمن بالله واليوم الآخر وعمل صالحاً من هذه الملل الأربع المؤمنين واليهود والنصارى، والصابئين.
فهؤلاء كانوا يدينون بالتوراة قبل النسخ والتبديل. وكذلك الذين دانوا بالإنجيل قبل النسخ والتبديل والصابئون الذين كانوا قبل هؤلاء كالمتبعين لملة إبراهيم الحُنفاء - صلى الله عليه وصلى الله على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما صلى على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم، إنه حميد مجيد - قبل نزول التوراة والإنجيل .
وهذا بخلاف المجوس والمشركين، فإنه ليس فيهم مؤمن . فلهذا قال الله تعالى : إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا وَالصَّابِئِينَ وَالنَّصَرَى وَالْمَجُوسَ وَالَّذِينَ أَشْرَكُوا إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَفْصِلُ بيْنَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ شَهِيدٌ ﴾ [سورة الحج : ١٧]. فذكر الملل الستّ هؤلاء، وأخبر أنه يفصل بينهم يوم القيامة. لم يذكر في الستُ من كان مؤمناً، وإنما ذكر ذلك في الأربعة فقط
.
/
ثم إن الصابئين ابتدعوا الشرك فصاروا مشركين والفلاسفة المشركون من هؤلاء المشركين وأما قدماء الفلاسفة الذين كانوا يعبدون الله وحده لا يشركون به شيئاً، ويؤمنون بأن الله مُحدث لهذا العالم ويُقرون بمعاد الأبدان، فأولئك من الصابئة الحنفاء الذين أثنى الله عليهم .
أول من ظهر ثم المشركون من الصابئة كانوا يقرّون بحدوث هذا العالم، كما كان المشركون بقدم العالم من العرب تُقرّ بحدوثه، وكذلك المشركون من الهند . وقد ذكر أهل المقالات أن أول من ظهر عنه القول بقدمه من هؤلاء الفلاسفة المشركين هو أرسطو .
The Fourth Station - Harran, the abode of the Sabians. For Harran was the abode of these Sabians, and in it Abraham was born, or he moved to it from his birthplace in Iraq, according to the two differing opinions. In it were the Temple of the First Cause, the Temple of the First Intellect, the Temple of the Universal Soul, the temples: the Temple of Saturn, the Temple of Jupiter, the Temple of Mars, the Temple of the Sun, likewise Venus, Mercury, and the Moon in Harran. This was their religion before the appearance of Christianity among them. Then Christianity appeared among them while those polytheist Sabians remained until Islam came. The Sabians and philosophers persisted there in the Islamic state until the last time. Among them were the Sabians who were in Baghdad and elsewhere as physicians and scribes, and some of them did not convert to Islam. When al-Farabi came to Harran during the fourth century, he entered upon them, learned from them, and took what the philosophers took. Thabit ibn Qurra had commented on Aristotle's words on metaphysics, and I have seen it and explained some of the corruption in it, for it contains much error. Likewise was the religion of the people of Damascus and others before the appearance of Christianity. They prayed facing the North Pole. For this reason, in Damascus there are ancient mosques with prayer niches facing the North Pole. Under the Umayyad Mosque in Damascus is a large temple with a prayer niche facing the North Pole that belonged to these people. The Sabians are of two types: monotheist Hanif Sabians and polytheist Sabians. The former are those whom Allah praised in His saying: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews and Christians and Sabians, whoever believed in Allah and the Last Day and did righteousness—will have their reward with their Lord, and no fear will there be concerning them, nor will they grieve.' So He praised those who believe in Allah and the Last Day and do righteousness from among these four religions: the believers, the Jews, the Christians, and the Sabians. These were followers of the Torah before the abrogation and alteration, and likewise those who followed the Gospel before abrogation and alteration, and the Sabians who were before these, like the followers of the religion of Abraham the Hanif—peace be upon him and upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad as He sent blessings upon Abraham and the family of Abraham, indeed He is Praiseworthy, Glorious—before the revelation of the Torah and the Gospel. This is contrary to the Magians and polytheists, for among them there is no believer. For this reason Allah said: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews and Sabians and Christians and Magians and those who associated with Allah—indeed Allah will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection. Indeed Allah is, over all things, Witness.' So He mentioned these six religions and informed that He will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection. He did not mention in the six any who was a believer; rather He mentioned that only in the four. Then the Sabians innovated polytheism and became polytheists, and the polytheist philosophers are among these polytheists. As for the ancient philosophers who used to worship Allah alone, not associating anything with Him, and believed that Allah is the Creator of this world, and affirmed the resurrection of bodies—those are among the Hanif Sabians whom Allah praised. Then the polytheists among the Sabians used to affirm the temporal origination of this world, just as the polytheists among the Arabs used to affirm its temporal origination, and likewise the polytheists among the Indians. The authors of doctrinal works have mentioned that the first from whom the statement of its eternity appeared among these polytheist philosophers was Aristotle.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a historical and doctrinal exposition by Ibn Taymiyya in which he traces the origins of philosophical doctrines, particularly the claim of the eternity of the world, back to the polytheist branch of the Sabians. The passage functions as a critique of the philosophers by showing that their core belief (qidam al-‘ālam) has a dubious origin. The author begins by describing Harran as the center of the Sabians, mentioning the temples dedicated to celestial bodies and abstract entities like the First Cause, First Intellect, and Universal Soul. This sets the stage: the Sabians were originally star-worshippers. He notes that Christianity and later Islam spread among them, but some Sabians remained polytheists. Importantly, al-Farabi studied with them, and Thabit ibn Qurra, a Sabian, commented on Aristotle’s metaphysics. Ibn Taymiyya claims to have seen this commentary and found it corrupt. He then shifts to the Sabians themselves, declaring that there are two types: monotheist Hanif Sabians and polytheist Sabians. The monotheists are those praised in the Qur’an (Surah al-Baqarah: 62) for believing in Allah and the Last Day and doing righteous deeds. They followed the original Torah and Gospel before abrogation, or the religion of Abraham before the scriptures. In contrast, the Magians and polytheists have no believers among them, as indicated in Surah al-Hajj: 17, where Allah lists six groups but does not praise any of them. Then Ibn Taymiyya explains that the Sabians later innovated polytheism, and the polytheist philosophers (including Aristotle) belong to this branch. However, the ancient philosophers who were monotheists and believed in creation and bodily resurrection are among the praised Hanif Sabians. Finally, he notes that the polytheist Sabians initially affirmed the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of the world, even the Arabs and Indians did so. The first to claim the eternity of the world (qidam) among the polytheist philosophers was Aristotle. Thus, Ibn Taymiyya argues that the doctrine of the world’s eternity is a later innovation, not an ancient truth, and comes from the polytheist Sabians, not the original monotheists.

Key Terms
الصابئة
الفلاسفة المشركون
قدم العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, who was the first to express the doctrine that the world is eternal?
A) The monotheist Hanif Sabians
B) The polytheist Sabians before Christianity
C) Aristotle
D) Al-Farabi

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's genealogical critique traces the doctrine of the world's eternity to Aristotle, who is linked to the polytheist Sabians, thereby denying it the authority of antiquity or monotheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a timeline in your notes: Polytheist Sabians (who believed in ḥudūth) -> Aristotle (first to claim qidam) -> al-Farabi (studied with Sabians) -> Thabit ibn Qurra (commented on Aristotle). Write a paragraph explaining how Ibn Taymiyya uses this chronology to undermine the authority of the philosophers.
?
Find one contemporary or medieval Islamic text that defends the eternity of the world (e.g., Ibn Sina's al-Shifā'). Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, criticize that text by questioning its historical origins. (Do not write more than 5 sentences.)

Constantine and the Innovation of the Christian Creed
Ibn Taymiyya traces Christian innovations to Constantine and pagan influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's claim that Constantine was the first to manifest Christianity and innovate the 'amanah' at the Council of Nicaea.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya traces the Christian creed to imperial innovation, not apostolic teaching.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya focuses on Constantine as the pivotal figure who transformed Christianity. He argues that the core Christian creed (al-amanah) was not revealed but invented by Constantine and his council. Let's examine how he builds this historical critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence where Ibn Taymiyya states that Constantine was the first king to manifest the religion of the Christians. Note the connection to the creed.
The claim is in the first few lines: 'Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians.'
2
Locate the innovation of the 'amanah'
Read the part about the 'amanah' that the Christians agreed upon in the time of Constantine. Identify how many scholars were involved.
It says three hundred and ten scholars agreed upon it.
3
Analyze Ibn Taymiyya's evidence
Note that Ibn Taymiyya does not provide textual evidence from Christian sources but asserts this as historical fact. Consider what kind of argument this is.
This is a historical claim based on his own knowledge of Christian history.
4
Summarize the critique
In one sentence, explain how this undermines the claim that Christianity is a revealed religion: it suggests human invention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - قسطنطين أول ملك أظهر دين النصارى
قُسْطُنْطِين أول ملك أظهر دين النصارى
وكان دين المسيح لما دخل فيه طائفة من أهل حرّان، وفيهم هيلانة الحرانية الفندقانية، فهواها ملك الروم أبو قُسطنطين، فتزوجها، فولدت له قسطنطين، فنصرت ابنها قسطنطين. وهو الذي أظهر دين النصارى، وبنى القُسطنطينية. وفي زمنه ابتدع النصارى هذه «الأمانة» التي اتفقت عليها طوائفهم اليوم، فإنه اتفق عليها ثلاث مئة وبضعة عشر من علمائهم وعبادهم . وقالوا : وهو الذي ابتدع الصلاة إلى الشرق. وإلا فلم يُصل قط أحد من أنبيائهم النصارى وأتباعهم إلى الشرق. ولم يَشْرَع الله مكاناً يصلي إليه إلا الكعبة . والأنبياء - الخليل ومَنْ قبله - إنما كانوا يصلون إلى الكعبة. وموسى صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن يصلي إلى بيت المقدس . بل قالوا : إنه كان يَنْصِب قُبَّةَ العَهْدِ إلى القبلة ويصلي إليها في التّيه . فلما فتح يُوشَعُ بيت المقدس بعد موت موسى نَصَب القبة على الصخرة، فكانوا يصلون إليها . فلما خَرِب بيتُ المقدس وذهبت القبة صارت اليهود يصلون إلى الصخرة لأنه موضعُ القبة . والسامِرَة يصلون إلى جبل هناك . قالوا : لأنه كان عليه التابوت . ولما رأى علماء النصارى وعبادهم أن الروم واليونان مشركون ، واستصعبوا نقلهم إلى التوحيد المحض، وضعوا لهم ديناً مركباً من دين الأنبياء ودين المشركين. فكان أولئك اليونان والروم يتخذون الأصنام المجسَّدة التي لها ظل فاتخذ النصارى الصور المرقومة في الحيطان والسُّقوف التي لا ظل لها . وكان أولئك يسجدون للشمس والقمر، فصارت النصارى يسجدون إليها، وجعلوا السجود إليها بدلاً من السجود لها.
The fourth station - Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians. Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians. And the religion of Christ had entered a group from the people of Harran, among them Helena the Harranite the innkeeper, and the king of Rome, father of Constantine, fancied her, so he married her, and she gave birth to Constantine for him, and she supported her son Constantine. He is the one who manifested the religion of the Christians and built Constantinople. And in his time the Christians innovated this 'amanah (creed) upon which all their sects agree today, for three hundred and ten of their scholars and ascetics agreed upon it. And they said: He is the one who innovated prayer towards the east. Indeed, none of their prophets and followers ever prayed towards the east. And Allah did not legislate any place to pray towards except the Kaaba. The prophets - al-Khalil and those before him - used to pray towards the Kaaba. Musa (peace be upon him) did not pray towards Jerusalem. Rather, they said: He used to set up the Tent of the Covenant towards the qibla and pray towards it in the wilderness. When Yushah conquered Jerusalem after the death of Musa, he set up the tent upon the rock, and they used to pray towards it. When Jerusalem was destroyed and the tent disappeared, the Jews started praying towards the rock because it was the place of the tent. And the Samaritans pray towards a mountain there. They said: because the ark was upon it. And when the scholars and ascetics of the Christians saw that the Romans and Greeks were polytheists, and they found it difficult to transfer them to pure monotheism, they established for them a religion composed of the religion of the prophets and the religion of the polytheists. So those Greeks and Romans used to take solid statues that had shadows, so the Christians took pictures painted on walls and ceilings that have no shadow. And those (Greeks/Romans) used to prostrate to the sun and the moon, so the Christians started prostrating towards them, making prostration towards them instead of prostration to them.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a historical critique by Ibn Taymiyya of the origins of Christian practices. He begins by identifying Constantine as the first Roman emperor to manifest Christianity and attributes the invention of the Christian creed (the 'amanah' of Nicaea) and the direction of prayer (eastward) to him. Ibn Taymiyya then argues that all prophets prior to Muhammad prayed towards the Kaaba, citing examples from Musa and Yushah. Describing Jewish and Samaritan practices after the destruction of Jerusalem, he points to the continuity of prayer orientation related to the Kaaba tradition. Finally, he explains the Christian strategy of mixing pure monotheism with pagan customs, such as substituting statues with images and shifting prostration from the sun and moon to towards them. The critique serves to highlight deviations from pristine monotheism.

Key Terms
الأمانة
قسطنطين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, how many scholars agreed upon the 'amanah' creed?
A) Three hundred and ten
B) Three hundred and thirteen
C) Three hundred
D) Three hundred and twenty

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the Christian creed was invented by Constantine and his council, not given by revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the passage again and identify another claim about Constantine's innovations besides the creed. Write a sentence summarizing that innovation.
?
Explain why Ibn Taymiyya mentions Helena's background (she was from Harran) and how that supports his critique of Constantine's Christianity.

The Innovation of Prayer Direction: East vs. Kaaba
Ibn Taymiyya traces Christian innovations to Constantine and pagan influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's argument that all prophets prayed towards the Kaaba and that the Christian practice of praying eastward is an innovation.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya claims the qiblah of all prophets was the Kaaba; Christians innovated the east.

Ibn Taymiyya extends his critique to the Christian practice of praying towards the east. He argues that no prophet ever prayed eastward; rather, they all prayed towards the Kaaba. By tracing the history of the qiblah from Moses to Judaism, he shows that the Christian innovation is a break from prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about prayer direction
Find where Ibn Taymiyya says that Constantine innovated prayer towards the east. Note that he says no prophet ever prayed that way.
The phrase: 'وهو الذي ابتدع الصلاة إلى الشرق' (He is the one who innovated prayer towards the east).
2
Trace the prophetic qiblah
Read the section that describes the qiblah of prophets: Abraham, Moses, Joshua, and the Jewish/Samaritan practices. Notice that all are connected to the Kaaba or its substitute (rock/tent).
The qiblah for all is either the Kaaba or the Tent of the Covenant aligned with it.
3
Understand the Judaic continuity
Ibn Taymiyya explains that after the destruction of Jerusalem, Jews prayed towards the rock (where the tent was), and Samaritans towards a mountain. This shows the original qiblah was not fixed eastward.
This reinforces that eastward prayer is a Christian innovation.
4
Evaluate the argument structure
Ibn Taymiyya uses a historical argument: since the prophets were consistent in their qiblah, any change must be a deviation. Reflect on the strength of this argument.

The fourth station - Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians. Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians. And the religion of Christ had entered a group from the people of Harran, among them Helena the Harranite the innkeeper, and the king of Rome, father of Constantine, fancied her, so he married her, and she gave birth to Constantine for him, and she supported her son Constantine. Syncretism: How Christianity Mixed Monotheism with Paganism
Ibn Taymiyya traces Christian innovations to Constantine and pagan influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's claim that Christian scholars deliberately created a hybrid religion by combining prophetic monotheism with Greek/Roman pagan practices to ease conversion.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya argues Christianity is a syncretic religion blending monotheism with pagan idolatry.

In the final part of the passage, Ibn Taymiyya explains the strategy of Christian leaders: they saw that the Greeks and Romans were polytheists and found it hard to convert them to pure monotheism, so they created a 'compound religion' mixing elements from both. This resulted in practices like icons and praying towards the sun/moon instead of prostrating to them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the motivation for syncretism
Find the sentence where Ibn Taymiyya says the Christian scholars saw that the Romans and Greeks were polytheists and found it difficult to transfer them to pure monotheism.
The phrase: 'لما رأى علماء النصارى وعبادهم أن الروم واليونان مشركون، واستصعبوا نقلهم إلى التوحيد المحض'.
2
Understand the resulting hybrid
Read what they created: 'وضعوا لهم ديناً مركباً من دين الأنبياء ودين المشركين' (a religion composed of the religion of the prophets and the religion of the polytheists).
3
Examine the specific pagan substitutions
Note two examples: statues (with shadow) replaced by pictures (no shadow); prostration to the sun/moon replaced by prostration towards them.
This shows a gradual shift from direct idol worship to symbolic veneration.
4
Evaluate the critique's impact
Consider how this explanation undermines the claim that Christianity is a purely divine revelation. It presents it as a human compromise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - قسطنطين أول ملك أظهر دين النصارى
قُسْطُنْطِين أول ملك أظهر دين النصارى
وكان دين المسيح لما دخل فيه طائفة من أهل حرّان، وفيهم هيلانة الحرانية الفندقانية، فهواها ملك الروم أبو قُسطنطين، فتزوجها، فولدت له قسطنطين، فنصرت ابنها قسطنطين. وهو الذي أظهر دين النصارى، وبنى القُسطنطينية. وفي زمنه ابتدع النصارى هذه «الأمانة» التي اتفقت عليها طوائفهم اليوم، فإنه اتفق عليها ثلاث مئة وبضعة عشر من علمائهم وعبادهم . وقالوا : وهو الذي ابتدع الصلاة إلى الشرق. وإلا فلم يُصل قط أحد من أنبيائهم النصارى وأتباعهم إلى الشرق. ولم يَشْرَع الله مكاناً يصلي إليه إلا الكعبة . والأنبياء - الخليل ومَنْ قبله - إنما كانوا يصلون إلى الكعبة. وموسى صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن يصلي إلى بيت المقدس . بل قالوا : إنه كان يَنْصِب قُبَّةَ العَهْدِ إلى القبلة ويصلي إليها في التّيه . فلما فتح يُوشَعُ بيت المقدس بعد موت موسى نَصَب القبة على الصخرة، فكانوا يصلون إليها . فلما خَرِب بيتُ المقدس وذهبت القبة صارت اليهود يصلون إلى الصخرة لأنه موضعُ القبة . والسامِرَة يصلون إلى جبل هناك . قالوا : لأنه كان عليه التابوت . ولما رأى علماء النصارى وعبادهم أن الروم واليونان مشركون ، واستصعبوا نقلهم إلى التوحيد المحض، وضعوا لهم ديناً مركباً من دين الأنبياء ودين المشركين. فكان أولئك اليونان والروم يتخذون الأصنام المجسَّدة التي لها ظل فاتخذ النصارى الصور المرقومة في الحيطان والسُّقوف التي لا ظل لها . وكان أولئك يسجدون للشمس والقمر، فصارت النصارى يسجدون إليها، وجعلوا السجود إليها بدلاً من السجود لها.
The fourth station - Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians. Constantine, the first king who manifested the religion of the Christians. And the religion of Christ had entered a group from the people of Harran, among them Helena the Harranite the innkeeper, and the king of Rome, father of Constantine, fancied her, so he married her, and she gave birth to Constantine for him, and she supported her son Constantine. He is the one who manifested the religion of the Christians and built Constantinople. And in his time the Christians innovated this 'amanah (creed) upon which all their sects agree today, for three hundred and ten of their scholars and ascetics agreed upon it. And they said: He is the one who innovated prayer towards the east. Indeed, none of their prophets and followers ever prayed towards the east. And Allah did not legislate any place to pray towards except the Kaaba. The prophets - al-Khalil and those before him - used to pray towards the Kaaba. Musa (peace be upon him) did not pray towards Jerusalem. Rather, they said: He used to set up the Tent of the Covenant towards the qibla and pray towards it in the wilderness. When Yushah conquered Jerusalem after the death of Musa, he set up the tent upon the rock, and they used to pray towards it. When Jerusalem was destroyed and the tent disappeared, the Jews started praying towards the rock because it was the place of the tent. And the Samaritans pray towards a mountain there. They said: because the ark was upon it. And when the scholars and ascetics of the Christians saw that the Romans and Greeks were polytheists, and they found it difficult to transfer them to pure monotheism, they established for them a religion composed of the religion of the prophets and the religion of the polytheists. So those Greeks and Romans used to take solid statues that had shadows, so the Christians took pictures painted on walls and ceilings that have no shadow. And those (Greeks/Romans) used to prostrate to the sun and the moon, so the Christians started prostrating towards them, making prostration towards them instead of prostration to them.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a historical critique by Ibn Taymiyya of the origins of Christian practices. He begins by identifying Constantine as the first Roman emperor to manifest Christianity and attributes the invention of the Christian creed (the 'amanah' of Nicaea) and the direction of prayer (eastward) to him. Ibn Taymiyya then argues that all prophets prior to Muhammad prayed towards the Kaaba, citing examples from Musa and Yushah. Describing Jewish and Samaritan practices after the destruction of Jerusalem, he points to the continuity of prayer orientation related to the Kaaba tradition. Finally, he explains the Christian strategy of mixing pure monotheism with pagan customs, such as substituting statues with images and shifting prostration from the sun and moon to towards them. The critique serves to highlight deviations from pristine monotheism.

Key Terms
دين مركب
توحيد محض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, why did Christian scholars create a compound religion?
A) Because the Romans and Greeks were already monotheists
B) Because they found it difficult to convert polytheists to pure monotheism
C) Because the Kaaba was destroyed
D) Because Constantine ordered it

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that Christianity is a deliberate syncretism of prophetic monotheism and pagan polytheism, designed for ease of conversion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify two specific Christian practices that Ibn Taymiyya claims were adopted from pagan Greeks/Romans. For each practice, explain how it was modified.
?
Imagine you are a Christian scholar responding to Ibn Taymiyya. Write a counter-argument (2-3 sentences) defending the use of icons as a means of worship, based on Christian theology.

The Unity of Prophetic Religion: All Prophets Were Muslims
Ibn Taymiyya asserts Muhammad's superiority and the unity of prophetic religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the textual evidence Ibn Taymiyya uses to support the claim that all prophets were Muslims and evaluate its doctrinal significance.

Core Idea
All prophets preached submission to Allah alone (Islam).

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya asserts the superiority of Prophet Muhammad and his nation, grounding it in the unity of prophetic religion. He argues that all prophets and their followers were Muslims, meaning monotheists who submitted to Allah. This is not a logical argument but a theological claim supported by Quranic verses and hadith. Understanding how he marshals this evidence helps us appreciate the Islamic epistemological framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the beginning: Ibn Taymiyya states that Muhammad is the imam of tawhid and that his nation is privileged over all who came before. He then says all prophets and their nations were Muslims, believers, monotheists. This is the central claim.
The claim connects Muhammad's superiority to the universal message of monotheism.
2
Locate the supporting evidence
Ibn Taymiyya cites three Quranic verses (Zukhruf 45, Anbiya 25, Nahl 36) and references a hadith from the Sahihayn. Identify each one in the Arabic.
These are the primary sources he uses to prove that all prophets called to tawhid.
3
Analyze the content of each verse
For each verse, note what it says: Zukhruf 45 asks previous messengers if they were worshipped, Anbiya 25 says every messenger was revealed that there is no god but Allah, Nahl 36 says every nation received a messenger to worship Allah and avoid Taghut.
All three emphasize the monotheistic message common to all prophets.
4
Understand the implication
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the religion of all prophets was the same: Islam (submission). This implies that there is no fundamental break between them; Muhammad's message is a continuation and culmination.
This supports his broader argument against those who see previous scriptures as entirely separate.
5
Recognize the rhetorical move
Ibn Taymiyya uses this scriptural evidence to counter any claim that previous religions were different or that polytheism was ever permissible. This is part of his critique of Greek-influenced logic that might treat religions as independent traditions.
The passage aims to establish a unified prophetic trajectory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضل محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم إمام التوحيد وأمته على من تقدم
ولهذا لما بَعَث الله خاتم المرسلين وأفضل النبيين محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم، إمام التوحيد الذي بعث الله به الرسل قبله وأظهره، وخَلَّصه من شوائب الشرك، فظهر التوحيد بسببه ظهوراً، فَضَّله الله به ، وفَضَّل به أمَّته على سائر مَنْ تقدَّم.
فإن الأنبياء جميعهم وأممهم كانوا مسلمين، مؤمنين، موحدين. لم يكن قط دين يقبله الله غير الإسلام وهو عبادة الله وحده لا شريك له كما قال تعالى : ﴿ وَسْلٌ مَنْ أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ مِن رُّسُلِنَا أَجَعَلْنَا مِن دُونِ الرَّحْمَنِ وَالِهَةً يُعْبَدُونَ ) [سورة الزخرف : ٤٥].
وقال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ مِن رَّسُولٍ إِلَّا نُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا أَنَا فَاعْبُدُونِ ال [ سورة الأنبياء : ٢٥]. وقال تعالى : ( وَلَقَدْ بَعَثْنَا فِي كُلِّ أُمَّةٍ رَسُولًا أَنِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ واجْتَنِبُوا الطَّاغُوتُ ﴾ [سورة النحل : ٣٦] .
وفي الصحيحين عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم أنه قال: «إنا معشر الأنبياء». وقد أخبر الله الأنبياء وأممهم - من نوح إلى الحَوَاريين ـ أنهم كانوا مسلمين مؤمنين، كما قد بسط في موضع آخر .
وقد قال تعالى : شَرَعَ لَكُم مِّنَ الدِّينِ مَا وَصَّى بِهِ نُوحًا وَالَّذِي أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ وَمَا وَصَيْنَا
The virtue of Muhammad, peace be upon him, the imam of monotheism, and his nation over those who came before. For this reason, when Allah sent the seal of messengers and best of prophets, Muhammad peace be upon him, the imam of monotheism with which Allah sent the messengers before him and made it manifest, and purified it from the impurities of polytheism, so monotheism became manifest through him, and Allah privileged him with it, and privileged his nation with it over all who preceded. Indeed, all the prophets and their nations were Muslims, believers, monotheists. There was never a religion accepted by Allah other than Islam, which is the worship of Allah alone with no partner, as He said: 'And ask those We sent before you of Our messengers: Did We make besides the Most Merciful deities to be worshipped?' [Surah az-Zukhruf: 45]. And He said: 'And We sent not before you any messenger except We revealed to him that there is no deity except Me, so worship Me' [Surah al-Anbiya: 25]. And He said: 'And We certainly sent into every nation a messenger, [saying], Worship Allah and avoid Taghut' [Surah an-Nahl: 36]. And in the two Sahihs from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) he said: 'We, the group of prophets...' And Allah informed the prophets and their nations - from Nuh to the disciples - that they were Muslims, believers, as has been explained in another place. And He said: 'He has legislated for you of the religion what He enjoined upon Nuh and that which We have revealed to you, and what We enjoined...'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya declares the superiority of Prophet Muhammad and his nation, emphasizing that Muhammad is the imam of monotheism, which he purified from polytheistic elements. The central claim is that all prophets and their followers were Muslims (monotheists). Ibn Taymiyya supports this with three Quranic verses (Zukhruf 45, Anbiya 25, Nahl 36) that ask previous messengers about polytheism, state the message of tawhid, and confirm that every nation received a messenger calling to worship Allah alone. He also references a hadith from the Sahihayn, though only the start is given, and mentions that this is elaborated elsewhere. The passage ends with a partial verse from Surah ash-Shura (42:13) about the shared religious principles. This argument serves to undermine the idea that previous religions were fundamentally different, reinforcing Ibn Taymiyya's broader critique of Greek-influenced logic as a deviation.

Key Terms
إمام التوحيد
مسلمين

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic verses and hadith to demonstrate that all prophets preached Islam (submission to Allah alone), establishing the unity and superiority of Muhammad's message.

How Ibn Taymiyya Proves All Prophets Preached One Religion
Author argues all prophets preached Islam, a single religion despite varied sharia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument for the unity of prophetic religion using Quranic evidence and the analogy of shir'ah and minhaj.

Core Idea
All prophets preached one din: worshipping Allah alone, despite differing sharias.

Ibn Taymiyya begins by asserting that all prophets were Muslims and their religion is one. He supports this claim with several Quranic verses that command the prophets to establish the din and not divide it. Then he addresses a potential objection: if the religion is one, why did different prophets have different laws (like the qibla)? His response uses the terms shir'ah (law) and minhaj (method) from Surah al-Ma'idah to show that the variety of sharias is like different doors and roads leading to the same goal: the worship of Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis
Locate the opening sentence that states the claim: 'All prophets were Muslims and their religion is one.' This is the proposition Ibn Taymiyya aims to prove.
The thesis is explicit: 'الأنبياء كلهم كانوا مسلمين، ودينهم واحد.'
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
List the verses cited: Surah ash-Shura (42:13) commands establishment of din; Surah al-Ahzab (33:7) mentions covenant; Surah al-Mu'minun (23:51-53) states religion is one; Surah ar-Rum (30:30-32) warns against division; Surah al-Baqarah (2:213) shows prophets sent to unite mankind. Note what each contributes to the argument.
Each verse reinforces the unity and preservation of the original din.
3
Examine the objection and response
The implicit objection: how can the religion be one if prophets had different laws? Ibn Taymiyya responds by distinguishing the core worship from its manifestations. Use the analogy from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:48): shir'ah (law) is like a door, minhaj (method) like a road – different but leading to the same destination.
The analogy resolves the apparent contradiction without minimizing the diversity of sharias.
4
Define the core of religion
Ibn Taymiyya distills the haqiqah al-din (reality of religion) as 'worshiping God alone without any partner' (‘ibadat Allah wahdahu la sharika lah). This is the essential element that all prophets agreed upon.
This definition is consistent throughout the passage and serves as the criterion for Islam.
5
Contrast with shirk
The opposite of haqiqah al-din is shirk. Ibn Taymiyya classifies disbelievers into two types: those who deny worship entirely (mu'attilah, like Pharaoh) and those who associate partners while acknowledging God as creator (mushrikun, like the pre-Islamic Arabs).
This classification underscores that the core of religion is exclusive worship of God.

Source Text

المقام الرابع - الأنبياء كلهم كانوا مسلمين، ودينهم واحد. قال تعالى: (شَرَعَ لَكُم مِّنَ الدِّينِ مَا وَصَّىٰ بِهِ نُوحًا وَالَّذِي أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ وَمَا وَصَّيْنَا بِهِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَمُوسَىٰ وَعِيسَىٰ أَنْ أَقِيمُوا الدِّينَ وَلَا تَتَفَرَّقُوا فِيهِ) [سورة الشورى: 13]. فأمر الرسل أن يُقيموا الدين ولا يتفرقوا فيه. وهؤلاء الخمسة هم أولو العزم، وذكرهم الله في آيتين من كتابه: هذه السورة وفي قوله: (وَإِذْ أَخَذْنَا مِنَ النَّبِيِّينَ مِيثَاقَهُمْ وَمِنكَ وَمِن نُوحٍ وَإِبْرَاهِيمَ وَمُوسَىٰ وَعِيسَى ابْنِ مَرْيَمَ وَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُم مِّيثَاقًا غَلِيظًا) [سورة الأحزاب: 7]. وقال تعالى: (يَا أَيُّهَا الرُّسُلُ كُلُوا مِنَ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَاعْمَلُوا صَالِحًا إِنِّي بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ عَلِيمٌ * وَإِنَّ هَٰذِهِ أُمَّتُكُمْ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً وَأَنَا رَبُّكُمْ فَاتَّقُونِ * فَتَقَطَّعُوا أَمْرَهُم بَيْنَهُمْ زُبُرًا كُلُّ حِزْبٍ بِمَا لَدَيْهِمْ فَرِحُونَ) [سورة المؤمنون: 51-53]. وقال تعالى: (فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفًا فِطْرَتَ اللَّهِ الَّتِي فَطَرَ النَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا لَا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ اللَّهِ ذَٰلِكَ الدِّينُ الْقَيِّمُ وَلَٰكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ النَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ * مُنِيبِينَ إِلَيْهِ وَاتَّقُوهُ وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ وَلَا تَكُونُوا مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ * مِنَ الَّذِينَ فَرَّقُوا دِينَهُمْ وَكَانُوا شِيَعًا كُلُّ حِزْبٍ بِمَا لَدَيْهِمْ فَرِحُونَ) [سورة الروم: 30-32]. وقال تعالى: (كَانَ النَّاسُ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً فَاخْتَلَفُوا) فَبَعَثَ اللَّهُ النَّبِيِّينَ مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ وَأَنزَلَ مَعَهُمُ الْكِتَابَ بِالْحَقِّ لِيَحْكُمَ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ فِيمَا اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ} [سورة البقرة: 213]. فالرسل - صلوات الله عليهم أجمعين - أولهم وآخرهم بعثوا بدين الإسلام، وهو عبادة الله وحده لا شريك له. يُعْبَد في كل وقت بما أمر أن يُعْبَدَ به في ذلك الوقت. فالصلاة إلى بيت المقدس كانت لَمَّا أمر الله به من دين الإسلام. ثم لما نهى عنه وأمَرَ بالصلاة إلى الكعبة صارت الصلاة إلى الكعبة من دين الإسلام دون الصلاة إلى الصخرة. حقيقة الدين فتنوع شرائع الأنبياء كتنوع الشريعة الواحدة. ولهذا قال تعالى: (لِكُلٍّ جَعَلْنَا مِنكُمْ شِرْعَةً وَمِنْهَاجًا) [سورة المائدة: 48]. فالسرعة الشريعة والمنهاج: الطريق والسبيل. فالشّرعة كالباب الذي يدخل منه والمنهاج كالطريق الذي يسلك فيه. والمقصود هو حقيقة الدين بأن يعبد الله وحده لا شريك له. وهذه الحقيقة الدينية التي اتفق عليها الرسلُ هي دين الله الذي لا يُقبل من أحد غيرُه. والشرك الذي حرمه على ألسن رسله: أن يعبد مع الله غيره. ومن لم يعبد الله أصلاً كفرعون ونحوه ممن قال الله فيهم: (إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِي سَيَدْخُلُونَ جَهَنَّمَ دَاخِرِينَ) [سورة غافر: 60]، فهؤلاء معطلة، وهم شَرُّ الكفار. ومع هذا يكون لهم ما يعبدونه دون الله، كما قال تعالى في قوم فرعون: (أَذَرْتَ مُوسَىٰ وَقَوْمَهُ لِيُفْسِدُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَيَذَرَكَ وَآلِهَتَكَ) [سورة الأعراف: 127]. فقال غير واحد من السلف: كان له آلهة يعبدها. ومن عبد مع الله إلهاً آخر فهو مشرك الشرك الأكبر الذي لا يغفره الله، وإن كان يعتقد أن الله وحده خلق العالم. وهذا كان شرك العرب، كما أخبر الله في غير موضع من القرآن أنهم كانوا يقولون إن الله خلق العالم، ولكن كانوا يتخذون الآلهة شُفَعاء يشفعون لهم ويتقرَّبون بهم إلى الله، كما قال تعالى: (وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُم مَّنْ خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ) [سورة الزمر: 38، ولقمان: 25]. وقال تعالى: (وَيَعْبُدُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ مَا لَا يَضُرُّهُمْ وَلَا يَنفَعُهُمْ وَيَقُولُونَ هَٰؤُلَاءِ شُفَعَاؤُنَا عِندَ اللَّهِ قُلْ أَتُنَبِّئُونَ اللَّهَ بِمَا لَا يَعْلَمُ فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَلَا فِي الْأَرْضِ) [سورة يونس: 18]. وقال تعالى: (وَالَّذِينَ اتَّخَذُوا مِن دُونِهِ أَوْلِيَاءَ مَا نَعْبُدُهُمْ إِلَّا لِيُقَرِّبُونَا إِلَى اللَّهِ زُلْفَىٰ) [سورة الزمر: 3]. وبسط هذا له موضع آخر.
The Fourth Station - The prophets, all of them, were Muslims, and their religion is one. He said, the Most High: 'He has ordained for you of religion what He enjoined upon Noah and that which We have revealed to you, [O Muhammad], and what We enjoined upon Abraham and Moses and Jesus: that you establish the religion and not be divided therein.' [Surah ash-Shura: 13]. So He commanded the messengers to establish the religion and not be divided therein. And these five are the ones of firm resolve, and God mentioned them in two verses of His Book: this surah and in His saying: 'And [mention] when We took from the prophets their covenant and from you and from Noah and Abraham and Moses and Jesus, the son of Mary, and We took from them a solemn covenant.' [Surah al-Ahzab: 7]. And He said, the Most High: 'O messengers, eat from the good foods and work righteousness; indeed I am, of what you do, Knowing. And indeed this, your religion, is one religion, and I am your Lord, so fear Me. But they divided their religion among them into sects; each faction rejoices in what it has.' [Surah al-Mu'minun: 51-53]. And He said, the Most High: 'So direct your face toward the religion, inclining to truth, [adhere to] the fitrah of Allah upon which He has created [all] people. No change should there be in the creation of Allah. That is the correct religion, but most of the people do not know. [And] turning in repentance to Him, and fear Him and establish prayer and do not be of those who associate others with Allah, of those who have divided their religion and become sects; every faction rejoicing in what it has.' [Surah ar-Rum: 30-32]. And He said, the Most High: 'Mankind was [of] one religion; then they differed. So Allah sent the prophets as bringers of good tidings and warners and sent down with them the Scripture in truth to judge between the people concerning that in which they differed.' [Surah al-Baqarah: 213]. So the messengers - may the blessings of God be upon them all, the first of them and the last of them - were sent with the religion of Islam, which is the worship of God alone, with no partner to Him. He is worshipped at every time with what He commanded to be worshipped at that time. So prayer towards Jerusalem was when God commanded that from the religion of Islam. Then when He forbade it and commanded prayer towards the Ka'bah, prayer towards the Ka'bah became from the religion of Islam, not prayer towards the rock. The reality of religion is that the varieties of the laws of the prophets are like the variety of the single law. And for this He said, the Most High: 'For each of you We have made a law and a method.' [Surah al-Ma'idah: 48]. So 'shir'ah' is the law, and 'minhaj' is the path and way. So the shir'ah is like the door through which one enters, and the minhaj is like the road which one travels. And the intended goal is the reality of religion: that God be worshipped alone, with no partner to Him. And this religious reality which the messengers agreed upon is the religion of God, which is not accepted from anyone other than it. And the shirk which He forbade on the tongues of His messengers is that one should worship along with God something else. And whoever does not worship God at all, like Pharaoh and others, about whom God said: 'Indeed, those who arrogantly scorn My worship will enter Hell in humiliation' [Surah Ghafir: 60], these are the mu'attilah (those who deny), and they are the worst of the disbelievers. Yet they still have what they worship besides God, as God said about the people of Pharaoh: 'Have you come to Moses and his people to cause corruption in the land and to abandon you and your gods?' [Surah al-A'raf: 127]. So more than one of the Salaf said: He had gods he worshipped. And whoever worships along with God another god is a mushrik of the major shirk which God does not forgive, even if he believes that God alone created the world. And this was the shirk of the Arabs, as God informed in more than one place in the Qur'an that they used to say that God created the world, but they were taking the gods as intercessors who would intercede for them and bring them near to God, as He said, the Most High: 'And if you ask them who created the heavens and the earth, they will surely say, 'Allah.'' [Surah az-Zumar: 38, Luqman: 25]. And He said, the Most High: 'And they worship besides Allah that which does not harm them nor benefit them, and they say, 'These are our intercessors with Allah.' Say, 'Do you inform Allah of something He does not know in the heavens or the earth?'' [Surah Yunus: 18]. And He said, the Most High: 'And those who take protectors besides Him [say], 'We do not worship them except that they bring us nearer to Allah in position.'' [Surah az-Zumar: 3]. And the elaboration of this has another place.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument by Ibn Taymiyya that all prophets were Muslims and preached a single religion, Islam, despite the apparent differences in their laws (sharia). It opens with a clear thesis statement at the 'Fourth Station' and then proceeds to support it with multiple Quranic verses. The author first cites Surah ash-Shura (42:13) which commands the prophets to establish the religion and not divide it, highlighting the five major prophets (Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad) as 'ulul azm' (those of firm resolve). He then quotes Surah al-Ahzab (33:7) about the covenant taken from these prophets. Next, Surah al-Mu'minun (23:51-53) is presented, where the messengers are told that their religion is one, but later people divided it into sects. Surah ar-Rum (30:30-32) emphasizes the fitrah (innate nature) of worshiping God alone and warns against division. Surah al-Baqarah (2:213) states that mankind was one community then differed, so God sent prophets with the Scripture. After these verses, Ibn Taymiyya summarizes that all messengers were sent with Islam, which is the worship of God alone. He then addresses an objection: the different laws, e.g., the qibla direction. He explains that worship at different times involves different commands, but the core religion is the same. He uses the terms 'shir'ah' (law) and 'minhaj' (method) from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:48) to illustrate that the variety of sharias is like different doors and paths leading to the same goal. The goal is the 'haqiqah al-din' (reality of religion): worshiping God alone. This religion is exclusive; no other is accepted. Then he discusses shirk (associating partners with God), which is the opposite. He categorizes non-believers into two types: those who worship nothing (like Pharaoh) — the 'mu'attilah' (deniers) — and those who worship other gods while acknowledging God as creator (the mushrikun of the Arabs). The latter believe God created the world but take intercessors. This, Ibn Taymiyya says, is the major shirk that God does not forgive. The passage concludes by noting that a fuller elaboration is given elsewhere. Note: All examples and quotes are from the Quran, illustrating the Islamic sciences (Tafsir). No secular examples are used.

Key Terms
الإسلام (al-Islam): The religion of all prophets, defined as worshiping God alone without any partner, and obeying His commands at each time.
الشريعة (al-shari'ah): The specific law or code revealed to each prophet; here analogized to a door, distinct but part of the single religion.
المنهاج (al-minhaj): The path or method of practicing religion; here analogized to a road, distinct but leading to the same goal.
الشرك الأكبر (al-shirk al-akbar): Major polytheism: worshiping another deity alongside Allah, even if one believes Allah is the sole creator; the unforgivable sin.
المعطلة (al-mu'attilah): Those who deny worship of God entirely (e.g., Pharaoh), considered the worst of disbelievers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the common 'haqiqah al-din' (reality of religion) that all prophets agreed upon?
A) Performing prayer towards Jerusalem.
B) Worshiping God alone without any partner.
C) Following the same set of legal rulings.
D) Believing that God created the world.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya proves prophetic unity by demonstrating that all prophets were commanded to establish worship of God alone, and that variations in sharia are merely different means to the same end.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, construct a short argument (2-3 sentences) to show that the differences between the sharia of Moses and the sharia of Muhammad do not contradict the unity of the prophetic religion. Cite at least one Quranic verse.
?
Classify the following belief according to Ibn Taymiyya's two categories of disbelief: 'A person believes that Allah created the world but prays to idols as intermediaries.' Is this mu'attilah or mushrik? Explain why.
